From the 
Chairman
 Business Report 2024
For 2024, the net profit was NTD 5.60 billion, compared to NTD 4.17 billion in 2023, an 
increase of NTD 1.43 billion. The EPS for 2024 was NTD 4.7, compared to NTD 3.5 in 2023, 
an increase of NTD 1.2.
Budget execution status: The Company’s main products are circuit boards and SMT assembly 
services. The circuit board production site are located in Luzhu and Dayuan in Taoyuan, and Huizhou 
and Fuling in China. In 2024, the sales volume was approximately 38.30 million square feet. 
The SMT assembly plants are located in Suzhou and Huizhou, China, with a production 
quantity of about 350 million pieces.
Research and Development Status: The Company continues to maintain its leading position 
in high-end circuit boards, primarily focusing on enhancing R&D to support the company’s 
long-term development capabilities and quality. It also strengthens information gathering 
from peers and suppliers, and continues to invest in research and development of new 
products and manufacturing processes, including satellite communications, AI servers, 
data centers, optical communications, AR/VR/smart glasses, humanoid robots, high-
frequency and high-speed material applications, water and energy efficiency improvements, 
environmental protection enhancement, smart factories, production safety improvements, 
automation upgrades, and manufacturing management enhancements, among others.
	Business plan for the year
Operational Policy
1. Actively develop blue ocean products and business related to satellite communications, 
AI servers, data centers, optical communications, AR/VR/smart glasses, and humanoid 
robots.
2. Continuously reduce variable and fixed costs in the management system, enhance 
contribution to increase profitability, and make products in all areas of the enterprise more 
competitive.
3. Strengthen the factory’s foundation, implement refined manufacturing management, ensure 
product quality, and enhance quality awareness among all employees. Ensure that the 
shipment quality meets customer needs and achieves a competitive yield level.
4. We will strive to fulfill our CSR, conform to the expectations of the government, our 
customers and society, continue to promote energy-saving and carbon reduction, protect 
human rights, improve employees' lifestyles and become a sustainable green enterprise.
●   Expected sales volume: Circuit board production bases are in Taoyuan Luzhu, Dayuan, and 
in China Huizhou and Fuling. SMT production bases are in Suzhou and Huizhou, China.
●   Key production and sales policies:
1. Rigid board products: Actively pursue orders related to satellite communications, AI 
servers, data centers, and optical communications.
2. Flexible and rigid-flex board products: Actively develop blue ocean products and pursue 
orders for AR/VR/smart glasses, humanoid robots, optical communications, and AI-related 
applications.
3. SMT Products: Continuously develop niche products and enhance the competitiveness of 
the factory's operational structure within the selected market products, enabling the factory 
to operate steadily.
Chairman and President 
P.K. Chiang
To all friends of Compeq:
In 2024, due to the impact of the ongoing US-China trade war, the easing of global inflation, and Fed interest rate cuts, the electronics market demand 
gradually recovered. According to IMF statistics, the global GDP growth in 2024 was 3.2%. The PCB industry, according to Prismark, saw a 5.8% 
increase in output value compared to 2023.
In 2024, the Company’s annual revenue was NTD 72.46 billion, an increase of 8.0% compared to NTD 67.08 billion in 2023. The net profit for 2024 
was NTD 5.60 billion, an increase of NTD 1.43 billion from the net profit of NTD 4.17 billion in 2023. In response to the high-frequency and high-speed 
applications of satellite communications, AI  servers, optical communications, and  data center-related products, the Company focuses on maintaining a 
robust structure, utilizing advanced big data and smart factory management to ensure product quality and delivery times, and establishing a competitive 
business management model.
In response to the intensified U.S. tariffs, intense competition in the Chinese market, and global economic uncertainties in 2025, the Company will 
adopt a conservative and cautious approach to address market changes. The Company will continue to enhance competitiveness while maintaining 
conservative and stable investments.
In the future, we will continue to optimize environmental protection, with an aim to surpass the legal and regulatory requirements. We will also implement 
corporate social responsibility (CSR) and concern ourselves with labor rights and interests to fulfill the expectations of shareholders, customers, and the 
government towards sustainable operations.
From the 
Chairman

From the

	Reporting Period and Boundaries
This report discloses data of our actions and performance in economic governance, 
environmental, and social aspects from January 1, 2024 to December 31, 2024, with 
the reporting boundaries focusing on plants (Luzhu Plant and Dayuan Plant) in Taiwan 
(collectively called Taiwan HQ), and also includes production sites in mainland China: 
Compeq Manufacturing (Huizhou) Co., Ltd. (Huizhou Plant), Compeq Technology 
(Huizhou) Co., Ltd. (Huizhou FPC Plant), Compeq Manufacturing (Suzhou) Co., Ltd., and 
Compeq Manufacturing (Chongqing) Co., Ltd. During the reporting period, the Company’s 
consolidated financial statements newly included COMPEQ (Thailand) (Thailand Plant). 
While the information disclosure scope does not fully align with the consolidated financial 
statements, the overall disclosure coverage reaches 99.1% of consolidated revenue. The 
remaining consolidated entities not included in this disclosure are primarily equity-invested 
businesses. Any changes in data compared with the previous version of the report are noted 
in the respective chapters.
	Reporting Guidelines and Principles
After gathering and collating various sustainability issues from home and abroad and 
investigating the material topics that concern various stakeholder groups through different 
channels, we prepared this report in accordance with the guidelines of GRI 2021 and 
disclosed the strategic goals, policies, commitments, and measures of material topics. 
We also prepared this report in accordance with the Moderate Assurance in Type 1, 
AA1000AS V3, to cover, as much as possible, the material sustainability issues that concern 
stakeholders and discloses information relating to ESG implementation. The assurance 
statement has been appended to Appendix IV of this report.
	Data Review and External Verification
The data and information in this report are provided by various departments and plants of 
the headquarters, compiled through daily operational management statistics and project 
discussions, and then compiled and edited by the CSR report preparation team. After 
generating the draft, it is reviewed through discussions with external consulting teams. The 
structure and disclosure directions were revised accordingly. After finalizing the draft, it was 
reviewed by the heads of each functional committee and reported to the Board of Directors. 
Once completed, it was publicly released on the Company’s website.
The collection, measurement, and calculation of various data and information for 2024 
comply with the local legal and regulatory requirements. When no local legal and regulatory 
requirements are available, the relevant international standards apply. When no relevant 
international standards are available, the industry standards and practices apply. The data 
has been verified by the third-party verification unit DQS (DQS Taiwan Inc.). Financial data 
has been audited and verified by the accounting firm Baker Tilly Clock, & Co. (information 
relating to financial performance is subject to the consolidated financial statements published 
after CPA certification). Except as otherwise stated, all financial data is expressed in New 
Taiwan Dollars (NTD), while other relevant performance is expressed in text or value 
according to internationally accepted indicators. Estimations and exceptions are footnoted in 
the report. Compared to the previous report, changes in this report are also indicated in the 
relevant contents.
This is the 15th report that Compeq Manufacturing Co., Ltd. (Compeq, the Company, or we) has published to disclose the status of our 
corporate sustainable development. This report has been prepared in accordance with the latest GRI Standards published in 2021 by 
the Global Report Initiative (GRI), the Technology & Communications-HARDWARE standards prepared by the Sustainability Accounting 
Standards Board (SASB), the climate-related financial disclosure framework recommended by the Task Force on Climate-related Financial 
Disclosures (TCFD), the Rules Governing the Preparation and Filing of Sustainability Reports by TWSE Listed Companies of the Taiwan 
Stock Exchange Corporation, and the Sustainable Develop Goals (SDGs) of the United Nations. This annual report (known as the CSR 
report before 2020) introduces in detail our sustainable actions and concrete achievements in major CSR areas, including economics, 
environmental protection, energy conservation, employee relationships, and social engagement in 2024 and explain to all stakeholder groups 
our engagement in sustainability issues.

 1-1. Compeq ESG and CSR Policy
COMPEQ Manufacturing Co., Ltd. is a specialist manufacturer of multi-layer PCBs and IC substrates. In addition to pursuing revenue and profit growth, we also actively implement CSR; engage 
in labor-management relations, employee care, corporate governance, environmental protection, and social welfare; emphasize legal compliance; protect the right to work; improve workplace 
health and safety; reduce environmental impacts; take social and environmental responsibility; and make ESG commitments so as to fulfill the expectations of stakeholders. To unfailingly 
practice CSR, the Board of Directors (Board) has approved the Corporate Social Responsibility Best Practice Principles and clearly defined the following four major principles: implement and 
promote corporate governance, develop a sustainable environment, maintain social welfare, and enhance CSR information disclosure as the guiding principles of CSR implementation. Through 
the Company’s official website, employee advocacy, and supplier commitment letters, Compeq communicates its responsibility toward society, the environment, and the economy, while 
encouraging stakeholders to actively participate.
Implement and promote corporate governance
Abide by international regulations and local laws 
and regulations that relate to social responsibility; 
continuously improve the rights, interests, and 
benefits of employees; establish an integral, 
healthy, and safe operational environment; and 
unfailingly implement social responsibilities.
Enhance information disclosure
Disclose information according to related laws 
and regulations and the “Corporate Governance 
Best Practice Principles for TWSE/TPEx Listed 
Companies, and fully disclose relevant and 
reliable information relating to corporate social 
responsibilities to enhance information transparency.
Develop a sustainable environment
Appropriately protect nature and the environment 
with respect to environment-related laws, 
regulations, and international standards, and 
maintain environmental sustainability while carrying 
out business activities and internal management.
Maintain social welfare
Abide by international regulations and local laws 
and regulations that relate to social responsibility; 
continuously improve the rights, interests, and 
benefits of employees; establish an integral, healthy, 
and safe operational environment; and unfailingly 
implement social responsibilities.
Compeq CSR Policy
E
S
G
●  Fulfill the commitments of our environmental safety policy as well as 
balance corporate growth with environmental protection to realize the 
goal of sustainable operations.
●  Maintain and promote long-term partnerships between the Company and 
employees, unions, stakeholders, and the local community.
●  Protect employees' human rights, ensure employee safety, promote the 
physical and mental health of employees, and protect the interest of 
employees and other stakeholders.
●  Conform to CSR-related international regulations as well as the labor, 
environmental protection and labor safety regulations set by the local 
governments to fulfill our responsibilities as a corporate citizen.
●  Comply with the ethics policy and respect intellectual property rights.
●  Assist suppliers and require them to meet the standards of the CSR 
policy.

1-1-1. Compeq ESG Sustainable Development Committee
To fulfill Compeq’s sustainability objectives and strengthen sustainability governance, in 2025, the Company established a Sustainable Development Committee under the Board of Directors, 
chaired by the Chairman, with a Vice President appointed as Chief Sustainability Officer to ensure the effective implementation of the Company’s sustainability initiatives. The Sustainable 
Development Committee is structured around five core functions: sustainable operations and risk management, sustainable project coordination, compliance, internal audit, and finance 
& accounting. Each function is led by the respective department head, who is responsible for advancing related sustainability policies and initiatives. The Committee regularly reviews 
implementation outcomes and makes ongoing adjustments to ensure the effectiveness of sustainability actions and measures, integrating them into daily operations. Furthermore, each plant’s 
top executive establishes a management system to ensure sustainability practices are effectively implemented. Compeq constantly monitors the development of domestic and international 
sustainability standards, regularly reviews and improves sustainability systems, and enhances effectiveness.

 1-2. Compeq’ s Response for UN SDGs
In 2015, the UN passed the 2030 Sustainable Development Agenda and officially announced the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) that include 17 SDGs and 169 targets. At Compeq, we treat 
sustainable development as a long-term operational concept and combine the SDGs with our business activities and development strategies. In the overall value chain, we include 17 SDGs in our 
consideration in materials procurement, manufacturing, and sales. Starting from the 17 sustainability issues requiring disclosure, we identified and addressed SDGs that are best connected with our 
core services. Lastly, 9 SDGs were selected as the focused direction of our future development. We will also continuously integrate SDGs to our organizational culture and routine operations.
SDGs
SDGs Corresponding Methods and Benefits
Corresponding Section
SDG 3: Good Health and Well-
Being
Promote a healthy workplace, 
develop health awareness 
in employees, and hire 
plant physicians to provide 
employees with consultation 
services about work, family, 
interpersonal relationships, and 
physical and mental health.
✓  In 2024, we arranged annual general health checkups, with targets covering new employees, active employees, annual 
health checkups, and special VIP health checkups. We also implemented graded management, follow-up, and health 
instruction.
✓  For high-risk employees’ health, regular outpatient blood tests are arranged to monitor (Glycated Hemoglobin, 
cholesterol, Triglycerides, liver and kidney functions).
✓  We share health issues each month for employees to understand their own health condition better and continuously 
follow up on various health anomalies.
4-9-12. Workplace Health and 
Safety Activities
SDG 4: Quality Education
Ensure inclusive and equitable 
quality education and promote 
lifelong learning.
✓  We value the education, training, learning, and growth of employees and plan a series of employee education and 
training courses.
✓  The average employee training was 33.2 hours per employee, with a total investment of NTD 5.059 million.
✓  Funding for the development of characteristic education at Sinjhuang Primary School (recorder ensemble), new 
comprehensive teaching building for Huizhou Huzhen Middle School, and Children’s Day activities at kindergarten 
amounted to NTD 5.650 million.

4-5. Employee Development and

5. Compeq Social Welfare
SDG 5: Gender Equality
Achieve gender equality and 
empower all women and girls.
✓  Employee salary and remuneration are determined based on their education attainment, experience, professional 
knowledge and skills, professional seniority and experience, and personal performance, regardless of gender.
✓  In 2024 the ratio of female to male employees was 39.5%, and there was no significant difference in the remuneration for 
women and men employees.
✓  We enforce the maternity health protection plan, maintain maternity protection and equality in employment for women 
workers, including interviews with health professionals, hazard assessment and control, and work ability arrangement.
✓  In 2024, the return to work and retention rates after parental leave in Taiwan were 96.6% (male 92.9%, female 100%).

SDG 6: Clean Water and 
Sanitation
Ensure availability and 
sustainable management of 
water and sanitation for all.
✓  We provide employees with safe, hygienic, and nutritional drinking water and institutional food, examine water quality of 
water dispensers every two months, and announce the examination results to ensure full compliance.
✓  We enhance the efficiency of process wastewater treatment to reduce environmental pollution.
3-6-4. Wastewater Management
4-9-6. Food Safety
SDG 7: Affordable and Clean
Energy Ensure access to 
affordable, reliable, sustainable, 
and modern energy for all.
✓  We continuously assess green energy installation and procurement, advance the search for green energy supply sources 
(build green energy/energy storage equipment/REC procurement/substitute fund payment), and increase renewables 
use each year. We also undertake to use green electricity up to 30% and reduce carbon by 30% (over 2024, base year) 
and make rolling adjustments by 2030.
✓  In 2024, the purchase of renewable energy exceeded 390 GWh, and solar panels were installed at the mainland China 
plant. By 2030, the goal is to increase the proportion of renewable energy usage to 30% (33.1% in 2024). The Company 
is actively assessing all markets to establish renewables business partnerships to enhance operational resilience.
✓  We implemented 171 energy-saving programs (41 for our plants in Taiwan and 130 in China). The total electricity 
consumption was 43,957 MWh, equivalent to reducing 24,379 metric tons of emissions.

SDGs

Goal 8: Employment and 
Economic Growth
Promote sustained, 
inclusive and sustainable 
economic growth, full and 
productive employment, 
and decent work for all.
✓  We abide by SA8000 and the RBA Code of Conduct (CoC), provide employees with reasonable pay and work conditions, 
eliminate discrimination, ensure equal work opportunities, protect labor human rights, ban child labor and forced labor, maintain 
employee health, and provide a safe workplace environment. In 2024, there was neither discrimination nor violation of labor 
human rights.
✓  We completed the version change certification of ISO 45001 and upgraded the OH&S risk control system to equipment safety 
management.
✓  Continuing to reduce major work injury risks, conducting safety observations and interactions on-site, promoting safety 
regulations through engagement, encouraging safety proposal incentives, and implementing ongoing improvements in areas of 
high risk identified in 2024, such as falling objects and ergonomics.
✓  We continuously implement the OH&S audit system and assign responsible employees to check and audit at different levels. 
Through the daily/weekly/monthly reports, the industrial safety unit conducts safety audits and ratings and reward units by 
performance.

 1-3. Stakeholder Engagement and Communication
To promote our sustainable development core concept, Compeq continuously communicated with stakeholders through various channels in 2024. Through communication in routine operations and the 
concerned issues under the international sustainable development trends, each year we conduct materiality analysis once, listen to the concerns about sustainability issues of stakeholders, locate the 
issues required for priority response in consideration of the nature of our operations, review the difference in understanding of each issue, draw up and implement corresponding medium- and long-
term improvement measures, and periodically review the progress and achievements to make rolling revisions for the reference of preparing our sustainability report and implementing sustainable 
governance. Apart from letting stakeholders understand our effectiveness in practicing sustainability, we also hope to make timely adjustments to our efforts in implementing corporate sustainability 
towards sustainable operations.
Identification of Stakeholders
In 2024, Compeq identified eleven categories of stakeholders, including employees, investors/shareholders, customers, 
communities, suppliers/contractors, media, government agencies, NGOs, labor unions, external consultants, and third-party 
verification organizations. Continuing from previous years, the stakeholder analysis follows the five key principles of stakeholder 
engagement standards (AA 1000 SES-2015) of accountability, responsibility, influence, diverse perspectives, and tension. The 
CSR team assessed the level of engagement with stakeholders and identified the key stakeholders for this year as employees, 
investors/shareholders, customers, labor unions, suppliers/contractors, NGOs/community neighborhoods, and government 
agencies. This is consistent with the stakeholder identification from 2023. Ongoing and ad-hoc communication channels are 
used to review engagement status. Issues of concern for each stakeholder group are incorporated into CSR daily operations and 
annual plans, and are addressed in the relevant sections of this report.
●  Understand the reasonable expectations and needs of 
stakeholders, and appropriately respond to their important 
issues of concern.
●  Consider the dual materiality and analyze the potential 
social, environmental, economic, and operational impacts 
of issues.
●  Make continual review and improvement to enhance 
sustainable performance.

distributed electronically to stakeholders. Based on stakeholder responses, 
relevant topics for Compeq’s sustainability report are identified and integrated.

 1-4. Identification of Material Issues
Identification and Analysis of Material Issues
After identifying key stakeholders, Compeq follows the GRI 2021 Sustainability Reporting Standards. Through steps such as identification, prioritization, confirmation, and review, the Company 
assesses stakeholders’ concerns about sustainability issues, the impact of these issues on Compeq’s operations, and their effects on the economy, environment, and society. Significant issues are 
identified, long-term sustainability goals are set, management policies and action plans are established, and performance is regularly reviewed through internal metrics. international trends, and peer 
comparisons. This process from the basis for the information disclosed in the report, proactively communicating our progress on sustainability goals to stakeholders and ensuring that their concerns 
are addressed in the report, continually responding to their expectations and suggestions.
Material Issue Assessment Process

3

6

Collection of sustainability-
related issues

of stakeholders

likelihood

17 sustainability issues

9 material issues

In accordance with AA1000 
SES, major communication 
targets were fully recognized 
and 7 major stakeholder 
groups were identified: 
employees, investors/
shareholders, customers, 
labor unions, suppliers/
contractors, NGOs/
community neighborhoods, 
and government agencies to 
discern the claims of different 
stakeholders.
Following the GRI, SASB, 
the FSC’s sustainability 
reporting guidelines, and 
specific issues related to the 
electronic components (PCB) 
industry, sustainability issues 
are collected as the basis. 
Each department also uses 
its business and operational 
experience to further 
investigate stakeholders’ 
concerns about various 
sustainability issues, allowing 
them to express their needs 
for sustainability information. 
A total of 17 sustainability 
issues are collected.
Through an online 
questionnaire survey 
targeting the seven major 
stakeholder groups, 305 valid 
responses were collected 
(a 38.1% response rate). 
Additionally, 201 experts 
consultations were conducted 
(such as customer surveys 
and industry information 
collection) to analyze the 
issues of concern for each 
stakeholder group and the 
level of attention they pay to 
these issues.
Following the GRI Standards 
(2021) definition of materiality, 
the internal sustainability team 
distributed a questionnaire 
to assess the impact of 
17 sustainability issues, 
considering the principle of 
double materiality. The team 
evaluated both the positive 
and negative impacts of 
these issues on the economy, 
environment, and people. 
Subsequently, the likelihood 
and impact severity of these 
events were assessed, 
creating a matrix of positive 
and negative impacts for each 
issue. This process allowed 
for the identification and 
ranking of the significance of 
each issue’s impact.
Analyze the stakeholder 
concerns and the positive 
and negative impacts of 
the issues (actual/potential/
positive/negative). Through 
cumulative scoring and 
ranking, nine material topics 
relevant to Compeq were 
identified, corresponding 
to 13 GRI specific topics, 
while also addressing one 
SASB standard (employee 
diversity and inclusion) and 
1 stock exchange issue 
(anti-competitive behavior). 
Determine the scope of 
information disclosure 
and develop management 
policies.
Track the accomplishment 
level and effectiveness of 
annual goals for material 
topics, dynamically adjust 
sustainability management 
actions, while non-material 
topics are addressed 
according to existing 
management processes 
and measures. Summarize 
key points, with detailed 
information disclosed in the 
report and verified by an 
external third-party unit. In 
the future, we will continue 
to review material issues, 
incorporate them into the 
Company’s management 
objectives, and develop 
departmental management 
strategies to continually 
enhance sustainability efforts.

Issue Impact Assessment Matrix
Each responsible department evaluates the impact of operational activities on the external environment, social groups (human rights), and economic governance. This assessment considers 
government regulations, customer requirements, and internal and external audit opinions. Departments score each issue based on the likelihood and level of impact, combined with stakeholder 
feedback on the level of concern, creating a matrix chart to illustrate the positive and negative impact of the issues.

Issue Ranking
By summing up the stakeholder level of concerns, positive risk ratings, and negative risks ratings, the issues are ranked.
● In assessing positive impacts, consider factors 
such as the likelihood of occurrence, compliance 
with regulatory requirements, exceeding 
regulations, or the ability to collaborate with 
customers to exert influence and create 
competitive advantages. Evaluate how each 
issue positively impacts Compeq, and continue to 
leverage corporate influence to generate greater 
sustainability value.
● In assessing negative impacts, consider factors 
such as the likelihood of legal compliance issues 
and the risk of actual or potential losses. Evaluate 
the overall negative impact of each issue on 
Compeq, and proactively develop response plans 
to mitigate potential risks.

Issue Selection
Through considering the Company’s sustainability strategy and focus area, the Company selected the top 50% of prioritized issues based on their ranking to identify the material issues for 2024, and 
choose 9 issues for disclosure. Other potential sustainability issues, although not included in the annual material issues, remain relevant to the Company’s operations. These issues will be highlighted 
and disclosed in accordance with GRI categories. We will responsibly disclose complete, accurate, and comparable information to enhance disclosure quality. The annual performance will be reported 
in the annual report and on the external website. We will continuously improve based on stakeholder feedback to maintain the trust of sustainability stakeholders.
9 material issues
Other Disclosure Issues

● Relevant disclosure indicators of SASB, ● Related disclosure indicators of Taiwan Stock Exchange Corporation
In the selection of material topics, certain issues were screened and consolidated, 
resulting in differences compared to 2023.
1. “Procurement practices” and “Supplier environmental assessment” were 
consolidated into “Sustainable supply chain management.”
2. “Customer privacy” was consolidated into “Customer relationship management.”
3. “Employment,” “Child labor,” “Labor-management relations,” and “Local 
communities” were not identified as material topics in 2024 due to a decline in both 
stakeholder concern and impact level. however, Compeq will continue to disclose 
relevant information on these issues.

Environmental Aspect
Air pollution
emission 
management
Emissions (305)
-
● Enforce carbon management 
and actively implement carbon 
conservation and carbon reduction 
programs to reduce GHG emissions 
from operations and enhance the 
resilience to cope with climate-
related risks. Plan the collaboration 
value change partners to reduce 
GHG emissions together and 
develop competitiveness for the 
low-carbon value chain.
● Through energy-saving and 
carbon-reduction measures, 
effectively manage GHG 
emissions while exploring new 
business opportunities (such 
as electricity-saving programs, 
replacement of outdated 
machinery, and self-built solar 
energy systems), thereby 
increasing revenue and reducing 
the risks and expenditures 
related to carbon taxes and 
fees.
● The government has announced 
regulations such as the Climate 
Change Response Act and 
provisions for major electricity 
consumers, mandating the 
establishment of carbon 
reduction and renewable energy 
targets. Due to the annual 
increase in renewable energy 
prices, the procurement of 
green electricity has become 
challenging, which will increase 
the costs of energy conservation 
and carbon reduction, as well as 
the imposition of carbon fees, 
resulting in financial impacts.
● Given the scale of 
manufacturing electricity 
use and the trend towards 
energy transformation, 
we continuously support 
government energy policies 
by installing solar power 
generation equipment and 
utilizing green electricity 
certificates. This enhances 
the proportion of renewable 
energy usage, attracts the 
attention of customers and 
investors, and creates more 
cooperation opportunities 
to improve market 
competitiveness.
● Extreme climate change 
policies and market 
changes may lead to rising 
energy prices, promoting 
stakeholders to demand 
higher standards for future 
sustainability. If demands 
for increased of renewable 
energy and reduced carbon 
emissions are imposed, our 
costs may rise. Failure to 
meet these demands could 
potentially affect customers’ 
willingness to place orders. 
Additionally, extreme 
weather events caused by 
climate change could lead 
to facility failures, such as 
disruptions or shortages in 
water and electricity supply, 
which would subsequently 
cause operational 
difficulties.

Waste

Waste 
Management 
(306)
TC-HW-410a.4
● Effectively control 
waste generated from 
operations, recycle 
waste and outsource 
disposal with appropriate 
methods. continuously 
promote in-house waste 
reduction, enhance the 
waste recycling rate, 
avoid the waste of 
resources and causing 
environmental pollution 
to gain benefits for 
developing the circular 
economy.
● Enhance the implementation of a 
circular economy (purchase costs, 
processing fees) and gradually execute 
zero waste policies in alignment with 
customer requirements to reduce 
waste generation and minimize 
environmental impact.
● Improper handling or transportation of 
waste may lead to leaks, posing risks 
to health and exposure to hazardous 
substances, which can result in 
fines for the Company, damage its 
reputation and increase disposal 
costs, thereby raising manufacturing 
expenses and reducing profitability.
● Promote material circularity 
through waste reduction and 
reuse to minimize waste 
generation and enhance 
resource efficiency.
● Improper handling or 
transportation of waste may 
lead to leaks, combined with the 
use of plant space for storage 
during incinerator maintenance, 
may pose risks to health 
and exposure to hazardous 
substances, which can result 
in fines for the Company and 
damage its reputation.

 1-5. Sustainable Performance of Material Issues
Material 
Issue
Management Approach
Management Target
2024 Performance
Long-term Goal (2030)
Operational 
Performance
1. Evaluate future business development plans on an 
annual basis according to the Company's global 
layout and industry overview, and forecast future 
market analysis.
2. As a listed company, we assess future business 
strategies through regular and irregular meetings 
(e.g., Board meetings).
3. Continuously enhance Board competence, improve 
the governance framework and information 
disclosure, ensure legal compliance, and enhance 
the trust in Compeq of stakeholders through the 
corporate governance roadmap.
4. Comply with all applicable international standards 
and local government laws and regulations, uphold 
ethical management policies, and respect intellectual 
property (IP) rights, including compliance with the 
labor laws and regulations and labor human rights, 
trade secret management, IP rights protection 
and management, information security protection, 
anti-trust laws, the US Foreign Corrupt Practices 
Act (FCPA), and fair-trade laws and related non-
disclosure agreements (NDAs). Encourage 
employees or stakeholders to seek assistance and 
appropriate advice through internal and external 
channels so as to file grievances for the early 
discovery and prevention of unethical behavior.
1. Continuously adjust product portfolios based 
on the operational strategy to accomplish the 
annual revenue target.
2. Continuously optimize legal compliance 
mechanisms and pay close attention to the 
government policy and legal changes in 
the sales locations to ensure compliance 
with local laws and regulations and no 
significant legal offenses and fines due to 
social, economic, and environmental non-
compliance.
3. Comply with the government’s latest 
corporate governance laws and regulations 
and connect with the international standards 
on “corporate disclosure of sustainability 
performance”. Enhance the external 
disclosure of ESG-related material topics 
and information transparency to effectively 
communicate with individual stakeholder 
groups and fulfill their expectations for 
Compeq’s sustainable appearance.
4. Establish a sound code of business conduct 
and ethics to ensure Compeq’s sustainable 
operations and prevent legal non-compliance 
and pay-to-play.
1. In 2024, operating revenue reached NTD 
72.46 billion, representing an 8.0% increase 
compared to 2023. net profit for the year was 
NTD 5.60 billion, with EPS of NTD 4.7, an 
increase of NTD 1.2 from 2023.
2. No significant incidents of corruption, ethical 
breaches, or ethical corporate management 
violations resulting in penalties have 
occurred.
3. No legal actions for non-compliance with 
anti-competitive behavior, anti-trust, and 
monopoly practices at home or abroad.
4. No government financial subsidies.
1. Continue to assess the domestic and 
overseas PCB markets, integrate strategies, 
enhance financial structure and cost-
competitive capacity expansion, and continue 
to enhance operational performance.
2. Continue with legal compliance, improve the 
performance in the corporate governance 
evaluation, and assess the increase in the 
seats for independent directors.
3. Enhance the disclosure and improve 
the quality of comprehensive ESG contents to 
continuously communicate with stakeholders.
4. No violations of corporate 
governance and ethical corporate 
management regulations (including ethics, 
corruption, ethical corporate management, 
and antitrust cases) have occurred.
5. Continuously promote the signing 
of ethical corporate management systems 
and provide education and training to 
enhance employees’ legal ethical corporate 
management and risk awareness, fostering a 
culture of honesty and trustworthiness within 
the Company.
Sustainable 
Supply Chain 
Management
1. Improve supplier compliance in labor human 
rights, occupational safety and health, 
environmental protection, business ethics, and 
management systems through the supplier 
sustainability evaluation mechanism and supplier 
social responsibility and ethical commitments. 
Suppliers shall take corresponding procurement 
countermeasures, conduct annual evaluations, and 
track deficiencies for improvement to reduce the risk 
of business interruption.
2. Develop local supply sources and establish 
prioritized cooperation relationships to increase 
the proportion of local procurement and reduce 
transportation carbon emissions.
1. Verify the legitimacy of suppliers through 
the selection mechanism to ensure their 
compliance with Compeq’s requirements 
in terms of compliance and ESG-related 
measures.
2. Increase the target proportion of local 
procurement to promote local economic 
development, reduce carbon emissions from 
transportation, and encourage the use of low-
carbon transportation measures.
3. Conduct ongoing supply chain 
sustainability assessments (including the 
signing of supplier social responsibility 
commitment letters and audits of high-risk 
suppliers) to ensure comprehensive ESG 
compliance throughout the supply chain.
4. Implement ethical and green 
procurement, ensuring 100% non-use 
of conflict minerals and compliance with 
hazardous substance regulations.
1. The local procurement ratio of the entire 
enterprise was 87.8%.
2. The completion rate for ESG, hazardous 
substances, and quality audits for high-risk 
suppliers was 100%.
3. All Compeq products complied with the HSF-
related laws and regulations and customer 
requirements. Maintained green procurement 
with zero conflict mineral or hazardous 
substance.
4. Conduct GHG inventory on key suppliers (25 
suppliers conducted independent inventory in 
2024, of which 16 suppliers were certified), 
and are encouraged to obtain ISO 14064-1 
GHG inventory verification.
5. Rate of improvement of audited 
nonconformities of suppliers is 100%, and 
no major deficiencies have been found 
that would result in the cancellation of the 
supplier's qualification.
1. Gradually increase the proportion of local 
procurement to support the local economy 
and community development, while reducing 
emissions from long-distance transportation.
2. Promote supply chain transparency and 
sustainability: Require suppliers to provide 
information on production processes, raw 
material sources, environmental and social 
impacts, and actively collaborate to advance 
sustainability in the supply chain.
3. Continuing to audit high-risk 
supply chains, we not only ensure legal 
compliance but also plan to collaborate with 
suppliers to reduce GHG emissions. The 
initiative encourages obtaining ISO 14064-
1 GHG inventory verification, leveraging the 
collective strength of the entire value chain, 
we aim to develop a low-carbon circular 
economy together.

Information 
Security 
and Privacy 
Protection
1. Establish the information security system and 
mechanism based on the framework of ISO 
27001, protect the security of corporate operations 
and services, and ensure authorized access of 
information to protect the rights and interests of 
customers and ensure the confidentiality of customer 
data.
2. Continuously plan and implement information 
security protection measures to accomplish the 
corporate goal of information security to engage in 
improvement, enhancement, and implementation and 
so to ensure business continuity through information 
asset inventory, risk assessment, and operational 
impact analysis.
3. Continuously raise information security awareness 
and strengthen employees' awareness of confidential 
data protection through information security training 
and MEMO promotion.
1. Ensure ISO 27001 certification across 
Compeq businesses
2. The Thailand Plant is expected to obtain in 
2026).
3. Continue to publicize and raise the concept 
and awareness of information security and 
update the depth and breadth of information 
security training contents to keep up with the 
times.
4. Continuously allocate budget for information 
security, including antivirus systems, EDR, 
vulnerability scanning, penetration testing, 
and hardware upgrades, in order to maintain 
and continuously strengthen information 
security.
5. No significant information security incidents.
1. Include information security issues in the 
education and training for new employees 
and remind employees of and publicize 
the importance of information security 
periodically.
2. There was no significant information security 
incident in 2024 (Losses exceeding NTD 1 
million).
1. Continue to pass the re-certification of ISO 
27001, with the Thailand plant expected to 
obtain certification in 2026.
2. In the future, we will actively integrate new 
AI technologies to automate detection and 
response to attacks, and rapidly identify 
potential threats through intelligent offensive 
and defensive mechanisms.
3. Maintain zero significant information 
security incident.
Customer 
Relationship 
Management

1. Establish an energy management mechanism 
to promote energy conservation and carbon 
reduction and reduce pollution emissions.
2. Implement low-carbon design in the

technology to reduce GHG emissions, and 
establish a carbon inventory system and plan 
internal carbon pricing.
3. Continuously implement the certification of 
the new-version ISO 14064-1 across the

1. Continuously introduce energy conservation 
and carbon reduction technology, upgrade

each year.

1 GHG inventory across the Compeq

Climate 
Change 
and Energy 
Management
1. Identify climate risks and opportunities with the 
Task Force on Climate-related Financial Disclosure 
(TCFD) as the framework, and formulate risk 
response and mitigation measures, with "net zero 
emissions" as the ultimate management goal, 
continue to promote climate change mitigation and 
adaptation plans, improve economic efficiency and 
reduce GHG emissions.
2. Voluntarily answer the CDP and CDP Water Security 
questionnaires every year to assess and manage 
environmental risks and opportunities and mitigate 
environmental impacts.
3. Enhance the operating efficiency of 
equipment and capacity through project management 
and data analysis and enhance resource efficiency, 
recycling, and reuse through source reduction to 
achieve the circular economy.
4. Set energy reduction targets each year 
and make rolling adjustments of GHG and energy 
management and the energy conservation and 
carbon reduction strategies.
1. Actively implement various energy reduction 
measures, use high energy-efficient 
equipment, and increase renewables use to 
optimize energy efficiency.
2. Propose corporate net zero emissions 
pathways and policies, periodically follow 
up on the results and make revisions, and 
connect with the government’s 2050 net zero 
pathway transition goal so as to achieve the 
goal of carbon reduction.
1. In 2024, the total electricity consumption 
of the entire enterprise increased by 8.4% 
compared to 2023, while the electricity 
consumption per unit of production value 
decreased by 3.6%.
2. Implemented 171 projects relating to energy 
conservation (41 in Taiwan and 130 in 
mainland China) in 2024 to save electricity 
by 43,957 MWh, equivalent to reducing 
emissions by 24,379 metric tons of CO2e, 
and an increase of 134.3% compared to 
2023.  
3. In Taiwan, the electricity saving rate 
reached 1.6% in 2023, as required by the 
Energy Administration, Ministry of Economic 
Affairs (the requirement was 1%). In China, 
energy consumption was controlled according 
to local dual-control standards (total 
consumption and intensity), meeting overall 
targets.
4. In the 2024 CDP climate change and 
water safety management questionnaire were 
both rated at management level B. 
5. No production interruption due to 
climate change disasters (such as typhoons, 
droughts, floods).
6. More than 390 GWh of renewable 
energy was purchased; plants in China have 
installed solar panels for power generation, 
accounting for 33.1% of total energy 
consumption.
1. Continuously reduce carbon emissions at 
the source (using low-carbon processes and 
fuels), manage energy targets, and implement 
energy-saving management plans for plant 
operations/processes, with a continuous goal 
of achieving 1.5% annual electricity savings 
and dual control of energy consumption.
2. Continuously deploy renewables, fulfill the 
government policies (Renewable Energy 
Development Act) in response to future 
development and legal and regulatory 
requirements. It is estimated to use green 
energy at 10% of Compeq’s capacity by 
2025. Compeq plants have started assessing 
relevant green energy projects (e.g., 
green power purchase) and increasing the 
proportion of renewables used every year.
3. Propose the enterprise-wide net 
zero emissions pathways and policies. The 
environmental planning and management 
team review the performance periodically. 
Targets include use of 30% of green power 
and reduce carbon by 30% over the base year 
(2024) by 2030.
4. Continuously optimize the quality 
of the TCFD-recommended climate-related 
financial disclosures and the CDP carbon 
disclosure information.

OH&S
1. Comply with or surpass the legal and regulatory 
requirements relating to occupational safety, set 
zero occupational accident as the target, and 
continuously implement OH&S management 
and supervision with respect to the ISO 45001 
OH&S management systems to eliminate hazard 
factors.
2. Continuously promote the “industrial safety 
for all” culture, encourage total participation to 
enhance safety awareness, and implement the 
preventive management and audit systems.
3. Supervise and review OH&S through 
communication with employee representatives 
or OH&S representatives and periodic OH&S 
meetings and encourage active engagement 
in OH&S activities with the intelligent safety 
management.
1. Zero occupational accident (excluding traffic 
accidents).
2. Full passage of the ISO 45001 certification 
across Compeq businesses.
3. Continuously encourage employees to make 
improvement suggestions and implement 
practical production training.
4. Include industrial safety self-inspection in the 
PAD check system for implementation.
5. No significant fines (over NTD 1 million) for 
non-compliance.
1. Maintain the continued effectiveness of ISO 45001 
across Compeq businesses, with the Thailand 
plant expected to obtain certification in 2025.
2. In 2024, a total of 75 external regulatory audits 
found no major fines (exceeding NTD 1 million) 
imposed on the Company. All equipment permits, 
testing, personnel certifications, and health 
checkups are continuously improved according to 
the PDCA system.
3. In 2024, a total of 531 industrial safety 
improvement proposals were submitted (382 from 
Taiwan plants and 149 from China plants), with 
bonus payments totaling NTD 251,000.
4. Conduct simultaneous self-inspections on high-risk 
behaviors (such as falling objects) and industry 
fire hazards, and establish comprehensive fire 
prevention measures, including cloud-based fire 
management SMS notifications and fire prevention 
education and training videos. Additionally, 
hold linkage meetings with on-site supervisors 
regarding occupational safety inspection items, 
requiring the implementation of the first-level 
autonomous occupational safety inspections.
5. There were no significant industrial safety 
accidents; however, there was one case of 
occupational disease. The industrial safety unit 
has conducted a human factors engineering risk 
investigation across various processes and has 
implemented control and improvement measures 
for high-risk items.
6. A total of 23 employee health management 
promotion activities (such as blood donation 
drives, body fat measurements, and bone density 
tests) were held, with approximately 1,771 
participants.
7. The follow-up rate for Taiwanese employees with 
abnormal health check results reached 89.4%.
1. Continuously implement the Occupational 
Health and Safety management systems 
through the PCDA cycle, pass the interim 
audit of ISO 45001, and maintain certification 
validity.
2. The number of safety and health cases 
involving all employees ≧ 500. Continuous 
efforts are made to promote hands-on 
occupational safety practices among all 
employees to enhance their willingness to 
participate in workplace safety.
3. Continuously conduct safety 
behavior observations and checks for high-
risk work points, along with safety awareness 
campaigns (such as human factors 
engineering assessment and improvement), 
and plan to establish positive KPI indicators 
for safety performance evaluation and 
rewards.
4. Establish relevant preventive 
mechanisms, implement design 
standardization, and comprehensively review 
maintenance regulations for fire damage 
prevention (such as safety inspections and 
improvements of electrical control boxes, 
thorough verification of equipment power 
wiring connections, and removal of unused 
equipment in ceilings).
5. Maintain zero major accidents, zero 
fatalities, and zero occupational diseases.
6. Follow-up rate for employees with 
abnormal health check results reached 100%.

Compeq continues to enhance its corporate governance practices by strengthening the governance structure and board functions, continuously improving risks management mechanisms, implementing 
operational supervision at all levels, adhering to ethical corporate management and ethical standards, and increasing stakeholder trust in Compeq.

 2-1. Company Profile
As Taiwans first PCB manufacturer that supports the governments policy to develop high-tech 
strategic industries, Compeq Manufacturing Co., Ltd. is headquartered in the Luzhu Plant, Taoyuan, 
Taiwan, and engages in the manufacture of printed circuit boards (PCBs), the key component for 
containing all electronic components and interconnecting the signals of electronics. Our product 
ranges cover general multilayer PCBs, high density interconnect (HDI) PCBs, high layer count (HLC) 
PCBs, flexible printed circuit (FPCs), and rigid-flex PCBs. In addition to the core PCB manufacturing 
business, we make revenue by offering surface mount technology (SMT) services at the request of 
customers.
2-1-1. Locations of Operations
2-1-2. Global Deployment and Services
The Company has been putting PCB manufacture as our core business since establishment. When China 
became the world’s factory after its economic rise, we established a production base in Huizhou, China, 
in 1996 to fortify our global deployment and Compeq Manufacturing (Chongqing) Co., Ltd. in 2013 to 
provide customers with the required mid-level and advanced PCBs after the government deregulated 
the restrictions on China investments so as to gain cost advantages, fulfill customer demands, and 
cultivate local potential markets. In view of the manufacturing process and production environment 
required of high level PCBs, an advanced plant with Class 1000 clean rooms was established in the 
Dayuan Industrial Park of Taoyuan County in 1998. The new plant is used for the development and 
mass production base of high precision products. To support the development of various customer 
products, in 2004, we established Huizhou FPC (Huizhou) Co., Ltd. and Compeq Manufacturing 
(Suzhou) Co., Ltd. to provide customers with flexible circuit boards and limited component assembly 
services and meet customers’ comprehensive needs.
In response to the rapidly changing electronic products, industrial ecosystem, and technology 
advancements, we make appropriate adjustments to the product structure and business deployment 
through constant review of the macro environmental changes to capture market opportunities and 
meet customer demands. Currently, the products used in the Company's circuit board production 
encompass various fields, including information technology (such as laptops, servers, peripheral 
devices, etc.), communications (such as mobile phones, tablets, base stations, etc.), networking 
(such as switches, routers, network storage devices, etc.), and consumer electronics. Additionally, 
Compeq integrates resources from its global production and service sites and the logistics support 
system of its corporate operations headquarters to continuously enhance its responsiveness and 
competitiveness, providing customers with comprehensive services from product development to 
after-sales support.
Technological capacity has always been one of Compeq’s key competitive strengths. We have spared 
no effort in developing new products and new technologies to meet the lightweight, slim, and small-size 
trends of electronic products. So far, we have developed precision and complex HDI technology (e.g., 
any-layer), flexible PCBs, and rigid-flex PCBs with a line with an interval at only 25μm, copper fill, 
and stack via. In view of the high-reliability requirement of advanced network equipment and server 
products, we have also developed the any-layer and high aspect ratio plating technology and PCBs 
using low Dk & low Df and high Tg materials.

2-1-3. Industry Overview
According to market research firm Primark, the market size of electronic products in 2024 is projected 
to grow by 6.9% compared to 2023, exceeding the previous forecast of 4.9%. This is primarily due to 
the server and data storage sectors growing by 45.5%, stronger than the expected 41.5%.
In the PCB industry, the total sales for the entire year of 2024 increased by 5.8% compared to 
the previous year, with an area growth of 6.8%. The overall Average Selling Price (ASP) of PCBs 
continued to decline in 2024.
For 2025, Prismark expects an overall growth of 7.4% in the electronic products market. Apart from 
the 12.1% growth during the pandemic rebound year of 2021, the growth rate projected for 2025 
is expected to be the highest peak since 2011, with the primary drivers remaining the server and 
data storage sectors. The growth rates for other product markets are approximately 2% to 5%, with 
the television market being the only one expected to decline. Demand for smartphones is projected 
to grow in 2024 and continue to maintain moderate sales growth in 2025. The improvement in 
communication infrastructure is primarily driven by increased demand for satellite communication 
services, while wired communication is also expected to grow in 2025.
In the PCB industry, Prismark expects a seasonal quarterly decline of 5.8% in Q1 of 2025; however, 
it will still represent the best first-quarter performance since 2021. The growth in 2025 depends on 
the strong increase in shipments of all electronic products except televisions. It is expected that the 
performance in high-end servers, data systems, and related fields will be particularly outstanding, 
thereby generating substantial demand for high-layer, multi-layer PCBs, and HDI.
2-1-4. Future Business Development Plans
For short-term business development plans, Compeq will continue to strengthen its focus on 
mainstream consumer products such as smartphones, tablets, and personal computers (e.g., AI 
smartphones, AI PCs, smart wearable products). In addition, we will actively develop key growth-
driving products, including data center and high-speed transmission products (e.g., AI servers, 
high-speed networking, optical module products), satellite communication equipment (e.g., space 
satellites, ground reception equipment), and automotive electronics (e.g., advanced driver assistance 
systems, autonomous driving, smart cockpits). Adopt a strategy of providing full product services for 
high-density interconnect (HDI) boards, high layer count (HLC) boards, high-density high layer (High 
Layer HDI) boards, flexible printed circuits (FPC), rigid-flex PCBs, and PCB assembly products, and 
to continue to invest in the technology development of these product lines.
In long-term business development, in addition to maintaining current mainstream products, we will 
also actively develop products with potential future growth and continue to engage in the research, 
development, manufacture, and customer service of these products, such as products for the robotics 
industry, quantum computing, and space exploration, provide customers with the best PCB-related 
products and services, and invest in more resources in a timely manner to develop and provide 
customers with related products and services.

Compeq has established a comprehensive technical R&D and production manufacturing system, 
with its R&D base located in Taoyuan, Taiwan. The Company focuses on the early-stage research 
and design verification of customer products. We place high importance on technological innovation 
and quality for the next three to five years, investing approximately 3% to 4% of our annual revenue 
in R&D each year. This investment aims to enhance R&D capabilities and quality, strengthen 
information collection from industry peers and suppliers, and continue the R&D of new process 
technologies, including satellite communications, AI servers, data centers, optical communications, 
and automotive-related products. Additionally, we focus on high-frequency and high-speed material 
applications, water and electricity usage improvements, environmental protection enhancements, 
smart factories, production environment safety improvements, automation improvements, and 
manufacturing management improvements. We actively monitor future product trends and position 
ourselves at the forefront of technology, committed to developing new products and technologies that 
meet customer needs. For 2024, we plan to continue investing approximately NTD 2.5 to 3 billion in 
R&D, with adjustments based on actual needs.

From the 
Chairman
●	 According to preliminary data from the International Data 
Corporation (IDC) Worldwide Quarterly Mobile Phone Tracker, 
the total shipments for 2024 increased by 6.4%, reaching 1.24 
billion units, marking a strong recovery after two challenging 
years of decline. We expect the market to continue growing in 
2025, albeit at a slower pace, as refresh cycles continue growing 
and pent-up demand is fulfilled.
●	 The strong growth witnessed in 2024 proves the resilience 
of the smartphone market as it occurred despite lingering 
macro challenges, forex concerns in emerging markets, 
ongoing inflation, and lukewarm demand. Vendors successfully 
adjusted their strategies to drive growth by focusing on 
promotions, launching devices in multiple price segments, 
interest-free financing plans, and aggressive trade-ins―fueling 
premiumization and boosting low-end devices―especially in 
China and emerging markets.
●	 While we remain optimistic about continued growth in 2025, 
the threat of new and increased tariffs from the new US 
administration has elevated uncertainty across the industry, 
driving some players to seek preventative measures to mitigate 
risks; however, thus far, the impact has been minimal.
●	 Additionally, due to the significant adoption of generative AI 
features, it is expected to drive the sales growth of AI smart 
phones. IDC expects that global shipments of AI-enabled 
smartphones will increase by 73.1% annually in 2025, reaching 
410 million units. The total global smartphone shipments 
are expected to be approximately 1.27 billion units, with AI 
smartphones accounting for about 32% of the total.
●	 Automotive electronics refers to the application of electronic 
systems and components in vehicles for various purposes, 
including vehicle control, safety, communication, entertainment, 
and connectivity. These electronic systems and components are 
designed to enhance the performance, efficiency, comfort, and 
overall user experience of automobiles.
●	 The global automotive electronics market size was valued at 
USD 259.6 billion in 2023 and is projected to grow from USD 
279.9 billion in 2024 to USD 425.2 billion by 2032, exhibiting 
a CAGR of 5.4% during the forecast period. Asia Pacific 
dominated the global market with a share of 43% in 2024.
●	 For the past few years, automotive electronics has been one of 
the highlights in the electronics industry, maintaining a stable 
positive growth of 5-10%. Intelligence and electrification are the 
two major trends in vehicles. Autonomous driving level is shifting 
from Level 2 to Level 2+/Level 3. Level 2+ has become the 
mainstream of today’s automobiles and is the main driving force 
for the self-driving automobile market. It is also the main product 
growth drivers for ADAS (Advanced driving assistance system).
●	 According to the statistics from Rho Motion, electric vehicle 
sales in 2024 will be 17.1 million units, an increase of 12.5% 
from 2023, accounting for 21% of overall vehicle sales. Looking 
forward to 2025, as the economy recovers, the demand for car 
purchases and replacements will also continue to grow. With the 
continue trend for electric vehicles, it is estimated that 20 million 
vehicles will be sold in 2025, a growth rate of approximately 
18%.
●	 The market research organization SkyQuest mentioned that the 
global small satellite market size in 2024 is approximately USD 
6.09 billion, with an estimated USD 6.82 billion in 2025. It is 
projected to grow to USD 14.54 billion by 2031, with a compound 
annual growth rate of 11.5%. Satellites, in addition to their 
traditional roles in scientific research, assisting communications, 
and positioning systems, are expected to drive the expansion of 
the global small satellite market due to the increasing demand 
for global communications and real-time data. The demand 
for small satellite solutions is constantly rising as more and 
more governments and commercial sectors inject funds into 
space technology. By supporting scientific research, national 
defense, and worldwide communication, small satellites promote 
innovations and sustainable use of outer space activities.
●	 The global small satellite market is dominated by the commercial 
end-use sector which needs better connectivity and data transfer 
as demand for satellite services such as broadband and Internet 
of Things is increasing. Investment in these constellations, 
which are driven by the demand for small satellite constellations 
facilitates advancements towards satellite technology and 
increases its commercial supremacy.
●	 In such a way that the communication app is taking the lead in 
global small satellite market as there is an increasing demand 
for data services and worldwide connectivity. This means 
that, especially in far-off and poor regions, the use of small 
satellite constellations increases due to their need for reliable 
and low-latency communication. As a result, investments on 
communication infrastructure have increased significantly which 
helps consolidate this dominance further.
●	 According to statistics from Canalys and TrendForce, 2024 global tablet and laptop shipments will be approximately 
148 million units, a 9.2% increase from 2023, and notebook computer shipments will be 174 million units, a 3.9% 
increase from 2023. 2023 market makes for easy year-over-year comparisons. A handful of device refreshes 
occurred during the recent quarters, and active channel filings were undertaken in preparation for major promotional 
events and the holiday season. Additionally, the integration of AI-related applications has contributed to overall 
sales growth, fostering an optimistic outlook for future development.
●	 Looking ahead to 2025, reduced political uncertainty following the U.S. presidential election and the Federal 
Reserve’s rate cuts are expected to stimulate capital flow. Combined with the end-of-service for Windows 10 
and demand for commercial device upgrades, Market research institutions TrendForce estimates global notebook 
shipments are predicted to grow by 2% to 177 million units in 2025. Among them, AI PC is estimated to be 100 
million units, with a growth rate of 100%.
●	 IDC expect tablets shipments to reach 153 million units in 2025, representing a year-on-year increase of 3.1%. The 
primary reasons for this growth are the replacement cycle of users who purchased tablets during the early stages of 
the pandemic and the market demand stimulated by upgrades in product performance and functionality.
●	 In 2024, the overall server market continues to experience rapid growth. According 
to market research firm TrendForce, the shipment value for 2024 is estimated at 
approximately USD 306 billion, representing an increase of about 53% compared to 2023. 
Within this total, the industry value specifically related to AI servers is estimated to be 
around USD 205 billion, showing stronger growth compared with the industry value related 
to standard servers. The increased procurement momentum from American and Chinese 
CSPs and server OEM customers is expected to drive a 46% year-over-year growth in total 
AI server shipments in 2024.
●	 Looking ahead to 2025, TrendForce estimates that the annual shipment volume of AI 
servers will increase by nearly 28% year-over-year. With the demand for AI servers 
expected to remain strong through 2025, and the average selling price (ASP) per unit 
contributing significantly, the market value has the potential to increase to nearly USD 298 
billion, further raising its share to over 70% of the total server market value.

2-1-6. Membership Associations
Upholding the belief in contribution and mutual growth, we actively participate in the unions and associations of relevant industries and maintain regular or irregular meetings and exchanges to improve our 
understanding of the trends, market information, and laws and regulations of the PCB industry so as to acquire new knowledge of the PCB industry and technology and establish sound collaboration with 
businesses and organizations in the relevant fields for the Company to keep up with the development of new technologies, accumulate energy for sustainable development, improve brand image, and increase 
market visibility. In 2024, we were a member of 13 business associations, industry associations, and alliances.

 2-2. Corporate Governance
2-2-1. Economic Performance
Compeq publishes monthly revenue reports, and holds corporate briefing and general 
shareholders' meeting every year. All relevant information can be found in the shareholder service 
section of Compeq's website (https://www.compeq.com.tw/accomplishments02_1.php).
Compeq's operating revenue in 2024 was NTD 72.46 billion, an increase of 8% from NTD 67.08 
billion in 2023. The net profit in 2024 was NTD 5.60 billion, an increase of NTD 1.43 billion from 
the net income in 2023 of NTD 4.17 billion. In response to the high-frequency and high-speed 
applications of satellite communication and 5G products, the Company focuses on maintaining 
a robust structure, utilizing advanced big data and smart factory management to ensure product 
quality and delivery times, and establishing a competitive business management model.

transparency and sustainable development. In addition to complying with the legal requirements 
of their locations and honestly disclosing tax information, all affiliates within the group report and 
pay taxes without delay and disclose tax information in the financial statement by law to ensure 
information transparency.

2-2-3. Corporate Governance Framework
Abiding by the Corporate Governance Best Practice Principles for TWSE/TPEx Listed Companies and the relevant regulations established by the competent authorities, Compeq implements corporate 
governance at different levels. In maintaining the rights and interests of stakeholders, strengthening Board competence, enhancing information transparency, and practicing CSR, we progressively 
implement various systems and regulations, keep improving the quality and effectiveness of corporate governance, and constantly maximize the rights and interests of shareholders and pursue sustainable 
operations.

2-2-4. Operations of the Board and Function Committees
The Board, Audit Committee, and Compensation Committee are operated in accordance 
with the relevant laws and regulations and exercise their powers according to the 
AGM resolutions. The Board has a diverse composition, with members coming from 
the management team, administrators of relevant industries, and accounting and 
financial professionals to effectively take the responsibilities of Board members with 
their different areas of specialization and backgrounds. These responsibilities include 
ensuring information transparency within the Company, delegating senior management 
officers, drawing up earnings distribution proposals, supervising and directing corporate 
operations, and requesting the relevant personnel to uphold ethics and integrity when 
carrying out duties to prevent damage to the Company and the rights and interests of 
shareholders. Additionally, climate change and environmental issues (such as greenhouse 
gas inventory and verification reports) are reported to the Board of Directors quarterly, with 
a total of four reports submitted in 2024.
Board Members
Board members are elected in accordance with the Company Act and the Regulations 
for Directorial Election. Chaired by the chairperson, the Board is seated by 5 directors 
and 4 independent directors. All are equipped with rich knowledge and a professional 
background in operational management. The academic attainment and experience of 
Board members are summarized as follows.

Board Diversity and Independence
To strengthen corporate governance and promote the robust development of the Board 
composition and structure, Board members are elected by competency regardless of 
nationality, gender, and age. As far as legal compliance is maintained, Board members 
are basically elected from those with PCB expertise, while other specialties, such as 
business administration, finance, human resources, and production and sales are also 
considered to strengthen Board competence in operational management, financial and 
accounting analysis, leadership and decision-making, and crisis handling accumulated 
by the relevant work experience of each Board member.
The specific diversification policy goals of the Company's board of directors: In 
addition to the consideration of the Company's daily operational needs, the proportion 
of all directors with PCB professional background should be more than 30%, and the 
proportion of independent directors with professional fields such as financial, business 
management, operations, and risk management should be more than 30%. To comply 
with the policy of advocating for the diversification of directors, one-third of the directors 
of either gender on the board of directors should be achieved
It is assessed that there are 10 directors and independent directors in the Company, 
of which 7 have PCB professional experience, which is in line with the company's 
principle of selecting directors with the PCB industry as the main body, and 4 
independent directors have work experience in the National University of Finance and 
Accounting, corporate finance and accounting, and PCB practical management, so 
the overall board of directors not only has the core knowledge of the PCB industry, 
supplemented by the business judgment capabilities, accounting and financial analysis 
capabilities, business management capabilities, crisis management capabilities, and 
decision-making capabilities accumulated by the expertise and experience of each 
director, etc., to achieve the goal of the diversification policy of the board of directors. 
However, since the term of office of all directors of the company will not expire until 
June 14, 2026, with the current female (independent) director, in the future, we will 
actively look for suitable candidates to serve as directors of the company in the next re-
election candidate list to comply with the requirement that one-third of the directors of 
either gender are achieved.

Board Performance Evaluation
In order to implement corporate governance and improve the functions of the Board of Directors 
and functional committee members, Compeq established the "Board of Directors Performance 
Evaluation Procedures" in November 2020. As required, the performance evaluation of the Board 
of Directors and functional committees is conducted once a year, and an Audit Committee has been 
established to ensure the quality of important business decisions was assessed by the Board of 
Directors at the end of 2025, and the results were excellent. Please refer to the annual report for 
details at http://www.compeq.com.tw/accomplishments02_1.php
Remuneration Policies for Directors and Managers
The Compensation Committee is operated in accordance with the relevant laws and regulations, 
such as the Securities and Exchange Act, and the “Compeq Manufacturing Co., Ltd. Articles of 
Organization of the Compensation Committee” to establish and periodically review the performance 
of directors and officers; assess the policy, system, standard, and structure of their compensation; 
and submit the recommendations for compensation to the Board for discussion.
The compensation of independent directors is fixed. The amount is determined with reference to 
the status of the industry of this Company, the degree and frequency of involvement of independent 
directors in routine operations, and the approval of the Compensation Committee and the Board. 
Independent directors carry out their duties in accordance with the relevant laws and regulations 
to supervise: the fair presentation of the Company ’ s financial statements, the appointment 
(dismissal) and independence and performance evaluation of certified public accountants (CPAs), 
the effective implementation of internal controls, the Company’s legal and regulatory compliance, 
and the control over inherent risks and potential risks; and implement the duties stipulated in 
the “ Articles of Organization of the Compensation Committee ” and “ Articles of Organization 
of the Audit Committee”. Both committees hold at least one committee meeting quarterly, and 
extraordinary committee meetings are held as necessary to exercise their due care as good 
administrators. For details on remuneration, please refer to the annual report at http://www.
compeq.com.tw/accomplishments02_1.php.
Attendance Status of Board Meetings
The Board of Directors of Compeq regularly submits operating reports, comprehensively explaining 
the Company's operational results during the period, and discloses the operation of the Board of 
Directors in the annual report. In addition, the Board of Directors is convened on a regular basis. 
A total of 5 meetings were convened in the most recent year. The attendance of directors and 
supervisors are as follows:

Directors’ Conflict of Interest Avoidance Mechanisms
Compeq has established conflict of interest avoidance regulations in its board meeting 
procedures. Directors with a personal or representative corporate interest in any meeting 
matters must disclose the key details of their interest during the meeting. If there is a potential 
conflict with the Company’s interests, they must recuse themselves from participating in 
discussions and voting. Additionally, they cannot delegate their voting rights to other directors. 
Directors are also required to self-regulate and avoid inappropriate mutual support to ensure 
the independence and fairness of corporate governance. There was no significant conflict of 
interest in 2024.
The Company’s 17th Board of Directors meetings for the 1st, 2nd, 3rd, and 4th sessions in 2024, 
and the 1st session in 2025, were held on March 7, 2024, May 9, 2024, August 8, 2024, November 
7, 2024, and March 6, 2025, respectively. During these meetings, when discussing the remuneration 
system for directors and managers, Chairman P.K. Chiang, director Charles C. Wu, Victor Lu, 
P.Y. Wu, and P.H. Wu, independent director Tzu Kuan Chiu, Teng Ling Liu, Y.C. Huang, and 
Ming Chuan Ko, each recused themselves from the discussions and voting regarding their own 
remuneration. The motions were approved without objection from the attending directors.
Operations and Members of the Remuneration Committee
Compeq’s Remuneration Committee aims to review the organizational charter of the remuneration 
committee and propose amendments as needed. The committee also regularly reviews the 
Company’s remuneration systems for directors and managers, and submits recommendations to 
the Board of Directors. The members of the Remuneration Committee are appointed by the Board 
of Directors and consist of three independent directors. The current term for committee members 
is from June 15, 2023 to May 30, 2026. The Remuneration Committee held 5 meetings in the most 
recent year. The qualifications and attendance of the committee members are as follows:

Compeq established an Audit Committee in 2017, as required by the FSC. The committee 
currently consists of 4 audit members, all of whom are independent directors. The committee
