Organizational Charter of Compeq Manufacturing Co., Ltd. ” This year ’s focus for the Audit 
Committee includes reviewing financial reports, assessing the effectiveness of internal 
control systems, corporate governance matters, revision to internal control systems, and risk 
management issues.

Management of Internal Audit and Prevention of Insider Trading
The Company’s Board of Directors has established an independent Audit Office responsible for inspecting 
and evaluating internal control systems. The office employs dedicated internal auditors who, in addition to 
meeting the qualifications required by the Securities and Futures Bureau, continuously pursue professional 
development in internal auditing. The internal auditors’ roster is updated annually as required by law. The Audit 
Office continues to audit and supervise various internal management functions to enhance the Company’s 
operational performance. In addition to discerning the Company ’s sales and financial conditions though 
periodic audit reports and financial statements, independent directors will communicate with the chief internal 
auditor and CPAs as necessary or at least once a year. For details on meeting communication matters, please 
refer to the internal audit section at http://www.compeq.com.tw/company04.php. Additionally, we uphold 
the ethical corporate principles to conduct business. To prevent the improper leakage of material internal 
information from affecting the Company’s stock price, we take precautionary actions in accordance with the 
“Management of Insider Trading Prevention”. We also include insider trading in our internal control system to 
facilitate insider trading prevention. In 2024, there was no fine for non-compliance with corporate governance 
or anti-corruption nor employee-related corruptions or violation of insider trading by directors or officers.

 2-3. Ethical Corporate Management and Legal Compliance
In May 2020, Compeq’s Board of Directors approved the Ethical Corporate Management Best 
Practice Principles, which explicitly prohibits accepting any improper benefits or engaging in 
actions that violate integrity or laws. Such principle requires all employees, managers, and 
directors to refrain from engaging in or instructing others to perform illegal and unethical actions. 
In 2024, relevant internal transaction precautions were promoted to 16 key personnel. With 
the ethical corporate management policy, we hope to provide an ethical standard for various 
business activities operated within the Company; specify the integral, fair, accurate, timely, and 
understandable disclosure of related accounting systems and internal control systems; announce 
the implementation of the code of conduct and anti-corruption, the measures for reporting unethical 
behavior and protecting whistleblowers against retaliation to provide suitable channels of reporting. 
We have also published important regulations and codes relating to ethical corporate management 
on the corporate website and employee portal for inquiries of outsiders and employees at any time.
Prevention of Ethical Corporate Management
Give and take bribes
Infringe on trade secrets, trademark rights, patent 
rights, copyrights, and other IP rights
Offer illegal political financing
Engaging in anti-competitive behavior
Make improper charity donations or 
sponsoring
Give or take unreasonable gifts, treatments, or other 
undue advantages
Handling Procedures
When the Company receives a whistleblowing report, it forms a special task force to investigate 
suspected illegal (including corruption) and unethical behaviors in accordance with relevant 
laws and regulations. The responsible unit protects and retains all related reports, investigation 
documents, evidence, and records.
Dedicated Handling Personnel
Assign dedicated personnel for different issues. The Company’s dedicated personnel include 
the Audit Office, HR Department, Legal Department, and other relevant departments. For specific 
cases. relevant individuals are invited to form a task force.
Reports and Rulings
If the investigation reveals illegal activities or improper conduct, the Company may take appropriate 
corrective actions, disciplinary measures, and/or legal actions. When necessary, it shall report 
to the competent authorities or refer the case to judicial authorities for investigation. If the 
investigation uncovers significant violations or if the Company is at risk of substantial damage, 
a report shall be made immediately, the independent directors shall be notified in writing, and 
appropriate rewards shall be given to the whistleblower.
(1) Employee complaint investigation record and case closure report
(2) Disciplinary actions will be taken for violations according to the “Work Rules” and “Reward and 
Punishment Procedures”
(3) Strengthen internal and external advocacy, education and training
Making signed 
or anonymous 
reports of facts
Starting investigation 
immediately after report

reasonable time.

for resolution after the

✓ Ensure the confidentiality of the identity of whistleblowers and prevent potential retaliation 
of involved parties.
✓ No employee will be discharged, transferred, or given unfavorable treatment of any kind for 
reporting unethical behavior.
✓ Obligation to ensure absolute confidentiality of the investigation and facts.
✓ Turning reported unethical behavior into teaching materials for constant outreach.

Establishment of  
Related Regulations
Training and 
Awareness 
Education of Ethics
Whistleblowing 
and Protection
Formulated the Ethical Corporate Management Best Practice Principles and Ethical Policy, which are published on the external website. 
Designed the "Supplier Social Responsibility and Ethical Code of Conduct Commitment Letter," clearly stipulating clauses on integrity 
conduct. These related measures are subject to revision based on scale. Additionally, the procurement contracts signed with suppliers also 
include aspects such as the RBA code of conduct, fair competition, and antitrust clauses. In 2024, there was no corruption or unethical 
behavior in major suppliers, and they also signed the supplier commitment.
Compeq also implements RBA training with classroom courses for new and in-service employees. Employees are required to sign the Code 
of Honest and Trustworthy Conduct, which is incorporated into an annual regular signing and retraining process. This is to ensure that 
employees fully understand the content of the Code of Conduct and actively prevent the occurrence of improper behavior risks. The annual 
signing rate was achieved at 100%, with a total of 19,738 participants completing the training in 2024, resulting in a 100% completion rate.
Establish the Unethical Behavior Report Handling and Whistleblower Protection Management Regulations and reward-punishment and 
grievance systems. It is the responsibility of all employees to report unethical behavior to the management through the relevant channels, 
while it is the Company’s responsibility to keep the identity of whistleblowers confidential during the reporting and investigation and 
protect them from unfair treatment and retaliation. If a case is confirmed after verification and brings significant economic efficiency to 
the Company, whistleblowers will be rewarded based on the actual situation. In 2024, there was no legal action or damage due to non-
compliance with ethical corporate management, anti-corruption, or anti-competitive behavior.
Ethical Corporate 
Management Actions
Legal Compliance
In addition to abiding by laws and regulations relating to corporate governance and ethical 
corporate management, health and safety, and environment and labor human rights of the 
competent authorities, Compeq established internal regulations of different locations of operations 
according to local laws and regulations, keeping constant track of the legal and business trends 
and movements at home and abroad to revise regulations in a timely manner and implement legal 
education. In addition to legal compliance, Compeq also complies with international standards such 
as SA8000, RBA, ISO 14001, and ISO 45001 to actively create a harmonious and friendly working 
environment. In 2024, there was no major violation (fines exceeding NTD 1 million).

Department or the Head of HR based on the content of the report)

 2-4. Risk Management
At Compeq we manage operation-related risks through the existing management 
organization and internal control mechanism. Based on own duties and functions, each 
functional unit identifies risks in various aspects and draws up management strategies and 
countermeasures for the prevention, reduction, and transfer of risks. Management of all 
levels also holds meetings to review the risks within their jurisdiction. When establishing 
various standard operating procedures and work instructions, in addition to including 
mechanisms related to risk management, we periodically adjust control mechanisms based 
on the changes in internal and external business environments to ensure the involved risk 
controls can be controlled.
Risk Management Policy and Mechanism
Compeq implements various policies through risk management methods and in coordination 
with relevant laws and regulations. We also establish various SOPs to effectively prevent 
and control risks in routine management, shape and deepen a risk culture, establish 
complete, transparent risk communication, and combine with the internal control 
mechanism to ensure effective control of operational risks related to business operations.
Emergency Response Mechanism
At Compeq, we enforce the emergency response mechanisms and measures stated in 
ISO 14001, ISO 45001, ISO 27001, and ISO 9001 and completed the certification of 
these standards. To reduce the risks and hazards of emergencies, we have established 
complete SOPs and regulations for handling emergencies and anomalies to take immediate 
action when an emergency breaks out to mitigate the impacts, quickly recover from the 
emergency, and ensure business continuity to meet customer needs.
Additionally, for safety emergency responses such as fire, gas leaks, liquid spills, odors, 
earthquakes, and radiation leaks, the safety emergency response measures, reporting 
procedures, command systems, and handling procedures for personnel within the plant 
are executed according to relevant environmental health and safety regulations. There 
is at least one annual full-plant emergency evacuation drill and fire drill to ensure the 
effectiveness of emergency response measures, making standard operating procedures 
more comprehensive. Regular drills of emergency response measures are conducted to 
effectively minimize risk and damage.
Risk Identification and Countermeasures
For operational, financial, and disaster risks, we assess their likelihood and the severity of 
their impacts on the Company (impact aspect assessment includes finance, operations, and 
employees). Then, we plan and implement corresponding risk management plans based on the 
balance of risk appetite and prevention costs. We also make rolling reviews of potential that 
changes from time to time of the likelihood and severity of risks to capture the effectiveness of the 
risk management plans and the relevant controls.

Corporate 
Governance 
and 
Economics
Strategic Risks and 
Operational Risks
1. The business management unit periodically reports strategic issues to the Board; lowers strategic risks through the participation, recommendation, and supervision of Board members; and 
continuously manages the annual policy and target achievement through the operational performance meeting.
2. We abide by national policies, laws, and regulations and timely adjust internal systems in coordination with legal changes to ensure legal operations. For the status of corporate operations, we 
regularly hold meetings of shareholders and investor conferences and regularly produce financial statements and sustainability reports to enhance the Company’s information transparency.
3. In 2024, there were no important changes in domestic and foreign policies and laws that would have a significant impact on the Company's business.
Legal Risks
1. The Legal Affairs Department takes charge of legal risk management and provides legal consultation and advice to handle the internal system, legal compliance, disputes and legal actions, 
investments, and merges and acquisitions.
2. We request all employees to sign the “IP Rights, NDA, and Trade Secret Policy Agreement” to strengthen IP right management and the non-disclosure concept to eliminate the risk of 
improper uses or breaches.
3. We identify compliance with relevant laws and regulations of various services to make adjustments in response to legal changes to ensure the legality and legitimacy of corporate operations.
4. With the contract system, we manage the status of execution of various contracts and control relevant risks. Through the seal/stamp management system, we monitor and manage the 
production, issuance, use, and cancellations of corporate seals and stamps to reduce the overall legal risks of the Company.
Information Security Risks
1. Following the advancement of network technology and the rapidly changing malicious cyberattacks, we have implemented the ISO 27001:2022 information security management system 
(ISMS) and timely update to the latest protection hardware and software to cope with threats in the external environment. We also conduct periodic risk assessment to reduce the risk of 
malicious cyberattacks to protect important corporate information assets. In 2024, there was no significant impact on finance and operations due to sci-tech changes and industry changes.
2. We issue memos periodically to publicize new knowledge in information security to enhance employee’s awareness of information security.
Credit Transaction Risks
1. Operation-related Credit Risks
• To maintain the quality of receivables, we have established the procedures for managing operation-related credit risks.
• The risk assessment of individual customers considers various factors affecting customer payment ability, including financial status, credit rating by rating agencies, the Company’s internal 
credit rating, historical transaction records, and current economic condition. We will also use credit enhancement tools in a timely manner, such as prepayment and credit insurance, to 
lower the credit risk of specific customers.
2. Financial Risk and Credit Risk: The Company’s financial department measures and monitors the credit risk of bank deposits, fixed-income investments, and other financial instruments. Due 
to the fact that the Company's trading partners and counterparties are all reputable financial institutions, and because the Company engages with multiple financial institutions to diversify risk, 
there is no significant concern about material credit risk concentration or performance issues. Therefore, there is no material credit risk.
3. Liquidity Risk: We manage liquidity risk to maintain the cash and cash equivalents required for operations, high-liquidity securities, and sufficient credit of bank financing to ensure the 
sufficiency of financial versatility.
Corporate Image 
(Reputational) Risks
Our stock affairs department takes charge of the collection of information and the disclosure and publication of material information and establishes the crisis response mechanism and simulate 
potential scenarios of operational risks that may affect corporate image to immediately active the response system at the first time. We have also appointed one spokesperson and one deputy 
spokesperson to disclose information on and for the behalf of the Company and exonerate untrue information over the material information platform so as to maintain the corporate image and 
optimize communication with all stakeholder groups. In 2024, there was no business crisis caused by corporate image changes.
Purchase or Sales Risks
1. In terms of sales, we have comprehensive customer groups and offer production and assembly services for complete ranges of PCB-related products. In addition to supplying products to 
customers, we also distribute products to the end-customers of customers, with multifaceted sales channels. After consolidation, our major clients had a higher sales proportion. In practice, 
we distribute different types of products to different customer groups, such as the customers and end-customers of assembly plants, to effectively disperse the risk of sales concentration.
2. In terms of procurement, the Company uses appropriate raw materials depending on the product specifications and requirements. For each type of raw material, there are planned primary, 
secondary, and backup supplies, so the risk of this aspect is quite low.
• The main raw materials of PCB are copper foil laminates/film/electrolytic copper foil/dry film and various electroplating chemicals. The Company’s procurement sources are mainly well-
known domestic and international manufacturers with whom we have long-standing and stable supply relationships.
• In 2024, due to fluctuations in the international markets for metals such as gold and copper, as well as basic chemical raw materials, and factors related to the supply and demand of 
PCB raw materials, the unit prices of PCB raw materials have also changed accordingly. Looking ahead to the PCB raw material market prices in 2025, in addition to being influenced by 
market supply and demand and changes in the international raw material market conditions, there are also uncertainties caused by the tariff war and the US-China conflicts following the 
inauguration of President Trump, making it difficult to predict.
Financial 
Risks
Capital 
Expenditure Risks
1. Compeq's only guarantees are for 100% held subsidiaries or investments. The risks are therefore limited and has led to no profit or loss to date.
2. Trading in derivative products can be authorized by the Chairman under our company's "Acquisition or Disposal of Assets Procedure" but our current policy is to only engage in long-term 
foreign exchange transactions for hedging purposes. Future trading in derivatives by Compeq will be mainly for hedging purposes as well. Trading for profit will be avoided to prevent major 
losses from errors in judgment.
Interest Rate 
Risks
From the past interest rate trends, we understand that interest rates are unpredictable. Hence, we will periodically assess the influence of future interest rate trends on our loan interest and 
timely adjust our financing policy.
Exchange Rate 
Risks
As most Compeq products are for export, receivables are mostly billed in the US Dollar. However, as payables are made mainly in the NT Dollar or Chinese Yuan, the exchange rates between 
USD and NTD and USD and CNY become the major source of our exchange gains or losses. Past exchange rate trends showed us that exchange rates are almost impossible to predict with 
any prediction. Natural hedging of asset against debt was therefore used where possible by Compeq last year. Pre-sale of USD at the forward rate was also used to reduce exchange risks. The 
hedging position is increased or reduced based on the trend of the USD exchange rate.
Inflation Risks
Currently, no serious inflation problem is found in Taiwan, and inflation brings no material impact to our gains and losses.

Environment

Environment Pollution 
Risks
1. We strive to improve the recycling and reuse of various resources (e.g., water reclamation and metal recovery for copper, gold, and silver), enhance pallet reuse, and introduce the waste reduction 
plan to reduce waste production and disposal.
2. We have established an environmental management system (EMS) according to ISO 14001, developed full SOPs, and accepted periodic external audits.
3. In addition to conducting GHG inventory and reduction plans, the highest-level managers of each production plant regularly review and adjust these plans each quarter. They continuously revise 
and set targets to ensure their achievement. The Company proactively discloses its execution results through various channels, including the annual ESG report published in August, customer 
surveys, and participation in the Carbon Disclosure Program (CDP). In 2024, there were no significant environmental, health, and safety incidents affecting the Company’s operations.
4. Continuously inventory the emissions of Scopes 1 and 2 GHG and have passed the ISO 14064-1 certification (Luzhu/Dayuan/Huizhou/Huzhou FPC plants). In 2023, we will expand the emission 
inventory to Scope 3 GHGs for full-scale inventory, verification, and disclosure, and will complete the same in other plants (Chongqing/Suzhou/Thailand) by 2027.
5. In addition to reviewing GHG emissions, water consumption, and waste total weight on a regular basis, we have established related policies and targets for periodic review and continual 
improvement in order to fulfill CSR.
• Each year, we inventory GHG emissions and energy consumption according to ISO14064-1 to capture the current status to verify our reduction effectiveness. We also hire a third party to run 
external verification.
• In water conservation, we continuously implement a process water consumption review and reduction plan, enhance claimed water reuse, and establish the water consumption audit system 
to increase the quantity of water reclamation. Based on audits of the on-site water control system, efforts are ongoing to reduce process water consumption, aiming to achieve a 1% reduction 
target.
• In terms of waste, waste produced from the manufacturing process is sorted into hazardous waste and non-hazardous waste by law. We have also established a responsible management unit 
according to ISO14001 to effectively capture the sources and output of waste to achieve the goals of waste localization, waste to resource, waste dispersal, and recycling maximization.
Climate Change  
and Energy Risks
1. In response to FSC’s Sustainable Development Roadmap, we periodically report the GHG inventory status, climate change response plans, and their performance to the Board for supervision 
and governance.
2. Regarding the financial impact of climate risks and opportunities, as well as other related countermeasures and subsequent transformation plans, we conduct simulation assessments through 
various policies and climate change models such as those from the IPCC. Currently, we analyze aspects such as the use of renewable energy (cost of purchasing green electricity certificates), 
increases in utility costs (additional electricity expenditures), carbon fee collection (additional carbon fee expenditures), and energy-efficient equipment replacements (regular equipment 
expenditures).
3. At the current stage, we have set a target to reduce carbon emissions by 30% and use 30% renewable energy by 2030. All plants in China have established the installation of solar facilities. To 
meet these goals, we have already purchased 393,000 Green Electricity Certificates (GEC) in China. The parent company continues to assess ways to purchase renewable energy, with an aim 
to achieve 10% green energy installation by 2025. Additionally, we continuously review energy-saving measures in our plants to meet the goals of using green electricity and reducing carbon 
emissions.
4. The entire enterprise continues to enhance equipment efficiency and improve raw materials while evaluating the possibility of using renewable energy. In line with our comprehensive carbon 
reduction goals and policy commitments, we have planned to purchase Green Electricity Certificates (GEC) to meet these targets. We are also evaluating the self-installation of solar power, the 
use of low-carbon energy sources (such as natural gas), waste reduction and resource recovery, process optimization, and the carbon trading market.
5. Due to climate change, water and electricity shortages are increasingly frequent. In electricity consumption, we will continue to make green energy installations. In water consumption, we will 
continue to implement water recycling and reuse. Currently, we have started addressing the overall environmental impacts. Huizhou and Chongqing plants have also started planning the use of 
renewables and green energy at the request of customers. In 2024, there was no shipping delay or supply disruption due to natural disasters.
Society and 
Human Rights
Labor and  
Human Rights Risks
1. The Company follows international guidelines defined in SA8000 and RBA-CoC to protect our employees. If there are any conflicting provisions then the more rigorous provision is adopted.
2. We have comprehensive grievance and communication channels in place, including email, mailbox, phone line, and labor unions. Employee feedback is addressed in accordance with the relevant 
regulations.
3. Periodic labor-management meetings, employee welfare committee meetings, and business review meetings are held periodically for direct communication between management and employees.
4. Compeq provides a range of comprehensive training programs based on our organization and roles. The head of each functional unit is responsible for defining the skills and knowledge required 
for personnel of all levels in their particular field. With the assistance of the training unit, these are converted into suitable training courses that give employees the professional skills and 
knowledge required to carry out their work. All employees are encouraged to actively share their knowledge and combine the results with the performance evaluation system in order to realize the 
goal of employee learning and the passing down of experience.
Occupational  
Safety Risks
1. Continuously obtaining the certification of the ISO 45001 OH&S management systems to meet the standards for providing a safe and healthy workplace environment and regular safety and health 
education and training. We also accept periodic system audits.
2. Conduct competence and practical education and training on industrial safety, promote safety behavior observation, improve equipment safety devices, and enhance employees' safety awareness 
and behavior correction to effectively reduce the risk of injuries. In 2024, no work-related fatalities were reported.
3. We implement contractor management and request contract suppliers and contractors to sign the HSE Policy Commitment to abide by the HSE regulations and reduce hazards and pollutions.
4. Provide health services and occupational disease prevention for medical personnel, plan diverse health promotion activities, and share monthly health topics to enhance the physical and mental 
well-being of employees.
Business Ethics Risks
We have established comprehensive grievance and communication channels for employees to report any behavior against the law or the Compeq Code of Ethics or corruption. When probable 
noncompliance (e.g., financial data fraud, theft of company property, embezzlement of corporate property, acquisition of undue advantages, abuse of authority, breaches of trade secrets), employees 
can file a report of such behavior. Disciplinary actions will be taken based on the severity of offense or reward will be given according to the Employee Work Rules and related regulations. In 2024, 
there was no non-compliance with business ethics.

 2-5. Information Security and Privacy Protection
Compeq values all stakeholders, including employees, partners, shareholders, and operational-
related information security and privacy. The entire enterprise obtained the ISO 27001:2022 
information security management certification in 2024 (with the Thailand plant expected to 
obtain certification in 2026) and passes annual reviews. This certification ensures mechanisms 
to protect intellectual property rights, including technologies, inventions, materials, and data, 
to prevent the leakage of trade secrets. Operate the information security management system 
using the PDCA model, including customer-required confidential data, project confidentiality 
agreements, etc., to ensure that relevant business personnel maintain confidentiality during 
business operations and protect customers interests. Conduct at least one internal self-audit 
and one external by an independent third party each year to ensure the Company implements 
the ISO 27001 management system. Revalidation is performed every three years to maintain 
ISO 27001 certification.
Organizational Structure of Information Security
1. The information security management representative and convener is the highest-ranking official 
in the Company’s information unit (Chief Information Security Officer). This role is responsible 
for reviewing information security policies and management procedures, technical specifications, 
and resource assessment. Meetings are held regularly or as needed to review information security 
management matters.
2. The execution representatives at each plant are appointed by the highest-ranking official in the 
Company’s information unit. They are responsible for coordinating the “Information Security 
Implementation Team” and the “Emergency Response Team” in executing information security-
related tasks. Their duties include providing early warning, monitoring information security status, 
and handling information security incidents.
3. The Information Security Implementation Team, composed of members appointed by each plant’s 
execution representative, established information security management regulations. promoted 
information security activities, implemented audit improvement recommendations, and annually 
reviewed risk assessment standards. The team effectively manages risks and prevents threats to 
information security incidents.
4. The Emergency Response Team, composed of personnel appointed by each plant’s execution 
representative, is responsible for coordinating and supervising the execution of tasks by key 
business process owners when significant information security incidents occur. The team also 
coordinates resource allocation to ensure rapid recovery. Additionally, regular drills are conducted 
each year for critical business processes or application system services.
5. The Information Security Audit Team, appointed by the information security management 
representative and convener, is responsible for auditing the implementation of the information 
security management system.

Information Security Continuous Operation Plan Drill
● Each year, a key business process or application system service is selected for drills to ensure 
the effectiveness of the “Business Continuity Plan” or “Disaster Recovery Procedures” and 
to ensure that relevant personnel are up-to-date with the latest status of these plans and 
procedures.
● Before the drill, the person responsible for each key business process or application system 
service should complete the “Drill Planning Form” in the “Business Continuity Plan Drill Activity 
Record”, arranging the planning and execution details. If necessary, each responsible person 
may request assistance from relevant business units, including outsourced vendors.
● During the drill, the RTO and steps required for restoring information and communications 
technology (ICT) services should be incorporated into the drill plan.
● Drills can be carried out only after the "Drill Planning Form" is approved by the head of 
information security.
● The drill results should be recorded in the “Business Continuity Plan Drill Activity Record” under 
the “Drill and Execution Handling Form” and submitted to the head of information security for 
review.
● In 2024, the drill was completed within the planned schedule, and the Company did not 
experience any significant financial losses due to information security incidents.

Implementation of Information Security Policy
Compeq requires employees and partners to adhere to information security policies 
while ensuring the protection of customers and internal intellectual property. 
Measures include:
✓	 Dedicated area management: Each unit within the plant has dedicated 
information areas that unauthorized individuals are not permitted to access.
✓	 Customer codes: Use internal customer codes to prevent direct leakage of 
customer information. During production, these codes are converted to internal 
part numbers to maintain confidentiality.
✓	 Correspondence management: Do not use customer names in correspondence 
to prevent unauthorized access by unrelated parties.
✓	 Employee training: Internal training covers Antitrust regulations, trade secrets, 
and patents introduction. Each employee signs the “
Employee Intellectual 
Property Rights Assignment, Confidentiality Obligation, and Information and 
Network Resource Usage Policy Agreement
” upon joining, ensuring that 
customer confidential information is not disclosed.
✓	 ISMS management: Adhere to Information Security Management System (ISMS) 
to prevent improper use, leakage, and alteration of data, thereby reducing risks.
✓	 Information dissemination: Monthly information MEMOs provide updates on 
information security, promote adherence to company information security 
policies, and monitor compliance among employees.
✓	 Handling of violations: In case of violations, actions will be taken according to the 
Company’s disciplinary procedures. In 2024, there were no complaints regarding 
the infringement of customer privacy or data loss, and no legal penalties were 
incurred for products or services.
✓	 Personal data protection: Personal data is used only within the necessary scope, 
with clear regulations for data collection, processing, and use. Data is not used 
for secondary purposes without prior written consent. There was no personal 
data violation in 2024.
✓	 Information security budget: Allocate an annual budget for information security, 
including antivirus systems, EDR, vulnerability scanning, penetration testing, 
hardware updates, vendor maintenance, and ISO 27001 audits. 
✓	 Information security collaborate defense: Join the “
Taiwan CERT/CSIRT 
Alliance
” and TPCA Information Security exchange meetings, participate in 
training courses, and receive information security alerts.
✓	 Regular exchange: Regularly attend information security vendor briefings, 
Cybersec Taiwan, and other events to stay updated on the latest information 
security developments.
We also include the NDA in the 
employment contract signed by 
employees to request them to uphold the 
non-disclosure obligation during and after 
employment.
The service regulations and non-
disclosure regulations are defined 
in the “Work Rules” to provide 
a dependable reference for 
employees.
A periodic risk scan is performed 
on computers, antivirus software 
is installed, and patches from the 
original provider are updated to 
enhance end-user protection.
Access control, system 
authentication, password 
control, access authorization, 
and USB access control are 
established and implemented.
The information security system is 
established to prevent computer viruses 
or malware or spying on confidential 
data and theft of confidential data 
through social engineering.
Awareness education of 
information security is 
arranged for employees 
every month to raise their 
awareness of information 
security.

Reporting and Handling Information Security Incidents
When an information security incident occurs, the Information Security Emergency Response Team promptly 
reports and addresses the issue, aiming to restore normal operations as quickly as possible. The team also 
collaborates with external information security resources, rapidly understanding security alerts and intelligence 
events, and enhancing and accelerating detection and response mechanisms. If any employee violates the 
information security policy, they will be disciplined according to the Company’s reward and punishment system, 
and this will be considered in performance management to reduce information security risks. The information 
security team also reviews the policy annually, updates is based on advancements in information technology, 
and requires all employees to sign and comply with it. In 2024, there were no complaints related to violation of 
customer privacy or loss of customer data, and no product or service violated the law and was subject to heavy 
fines.

 2-6. Customer Relationship Management
Compeq’s business model does not target end consumers. Therefore, it currently focuses on ensuring 
that the goods and services provided, as well as the actions related to payments, procurement 
acceptance and payment, comply with agreements and legal regulations between the parties and legal 
requirements.
Customer Service
Compeq follows the principle of "Quality First, Customer First" and continues to improve our 
cooperation with customers. We assign an exclusive team for all customers to take charge of 
business undertaking, quality, delivery, cost, and after-sales service; propose counteractions and 
overall solutions for customer questions and feedback; conduct questionnaire surveys on customer 
satisfaction; and make continual improvement according to customer advice to enhance the loyalty 
of existing customers, recruit potential new customers, and thereby increase profit.
Compeq is committed to implementing the automotive industry quality management system 
(IATF 16949), the quality management system (ISO 9001), the hazardous substances process 
management system (QC 080000), and the aerospace quality management system (AS9100). The 
Company focuses on ensuring quality for its customer by continuously reviewing and improving 
through the PDCA concept, developing customer-oriented quality management system, and 
accomplishing comprehensive quality targets.
The Company designated a product general manager or a dedicated contact person for 
each customer to maintain regular communication, stay updated on customer dynamics, and 
ensure both parties’ best interests through effective negotiation mechanisms.
Customer Rights Protection Policy
1. Ensure that the product or service provided is consistent with the agreement between the parties 
and legal requirements.
2. Provide correct and clear information related to the content, maintenance, storage and disposal 
of the product or service if possible so that customers make fully-informed decisions.
3. Provide transparent and effective customer complaint procedures to fairly and promptly resolve 
complaints without undue burden or unfairness.
4. Not to engage in any deception, misdirection, fraud or unfair statement or omission, or any other 
improper acts.

Customer Satisfaction Survey
Compeq ’s business units conduct annual satisfaction surveys for major customers. Through 
statistical analysis, they review and monitor factors affecting customer satisfaction, including 
product technology development, quality, delivery time, pricing, and the presence of hazardous 
substances. Based on the survey results, the sales units prepare review reports and develop 
improvement plans. In 2024, customer satisfaction scored 88.3 points. Over the past three years, 
customer satisfaction has improved annually, aiming to reach 90 points. Additionally, there were no 
significant fines for violating service-related regulations in 2024.
The Company maintains regular contact with customers through designated product managers 
or specialized personnel. Customers can also use service platform available on the Company’s 
website (ServiceS00@compeq.com.tw) to submit suggestions and requests, continuously 
improving customer relations. We will further strengthen the close collaboration among internal 
departments to address urgent or unexpected customer needs. We are committed to constantly 
improving product quality, enhancing the timeliness and effectiveness of communication with 
customers, and maintaining good communication to meet customer requirements to the best of our 
ability.
2-7-1. Regulations for Sustainable Supply Chain Management (SCM)
Compeq’s supply chain management is guided by the Responsible Business Alliance (RBA) guidelines. 
We have established a “ Supplier Social Responsibility and Ethical Code of Conduct Commitment 
Letter ” that requires all suppliers to fully comply with the RBA guidelines and the Code, covering 
labor rights, health and safety, environmental, business ethics, and management systems, as well as 
adhering to local laws. We continuously promote compliance with CSR standards through supplier self-
assessments. We aim for our suppliers to achieve certifications such as SA8000, RBA, ISO 45001, ISO 
14001, and ISO 14064-1, thereby enhancing corporate social impact and promoting ESG balance and 
sustainable development.
In product manufacturing, for the products and raw materials provided by suppliers, we have 
established the “Commitment to No Use of Prohibited/Restricted Substances Specified in Related 
Environmental Regulations”, restricted substance regulations, and conflict mineral management 
policy.
Customer Grievance Mechanism and Handling
Compeq is committed to improving product quality and responding quickly to customer quality issues. 
In addition to grasping relevant information and understanding the reasons and requirements for 
complaints, we track and analyze the progress based on the urgency of each case. We compile 
complaint reports within the deadlines to ensure that all complaints are properly addressed and 
responded to.

 2-7. Sustainable Supply Chain
Suppliers are Compeq’s important partners. Therefore, we are committed to developing long-
term cooperation with suppliers, hoping to build a steadily growing sustainable supply chain. In 
addition to technology, product quality, and delivery punctuality, we urge suppliers to meet the CSR 
standards, improve health and safety, protect the environment, and value labor human rights to 
optimize risk management and the business continuity plan.

Supply Chain Status
Due to the complex characteristics of Compeq’s products, the supply chain includes various types 
such as raw materials, equipment, environmental services (waste disposal), manpower dispatch 
agencies, migrant labor agencies, and service providers (e.g., security). The Company has a total 
of 3,036 suppliers, with raw materials and equipment suppliers being the main categories. There 
were no significant changes to the supply chain in 2024.

Local Procurement and Key Suppliers
Compeq believes that local procurement is a key component of sustainable operations. We 
actively collaborate with our supplier partners to implement local procurement, which helps 
reduce unnecessary air and sea transportation costs and lower carbon footprints associated with 
transportation. This approach shortens product lead times, reduces the environmental impact of 
raw materials used in manufacturing, and indirectly creates job opportunities. Therefore, Compeq 
has dedicated procurement units at each location responsible for selecting and managing local 
suppliers.

In response to the structure and type of products, Compeq has a large number of suppliers. 
To effectively manage suppliers, 686 key suppliers were identified in 2024 based on principles 
such as procurement amount, key components, influence, uniqueness, and high-pollution 
industries. These suppliers were evaluated and selected using social, economic, and 
environmental indicators. The labor rights, environmental protection, and health and safety of 
the supply chain are subject to risk control. For the risks identified, different management and 
monitoring mechanisms are established for both new and existing suppliers.
Supply Chain Identification and Risk Assessment
We use the RBA Code of Conduct for managing supplier ESG aspects. This includes stages 
such as introduction, assessment, confirmation, and continuous improvement. Through these 
management measures, we collaboratively work on ESG issues to build sustainable supply 
chain. All cooperating suppliers must sign a “
Supplier Social Responsibility and Ethical 
Standards Commitment” declaration.
Through the "Supplier Social Responsibility Management Self-Assessment Form," suppliers 
conduct self-evaluations on various risk aspects including labor, health and safety, 
environment, ethics, and management systems. Based on the self-assessment results, the 
compliance status of suppliers in ESG aspects is confirmed, identifying the level of threats 
and impacts each supplier may pose to Hua Tong's operations. Regular on-site audits 
are conducted accordingly. In 2024, a total of 298 high-risk suppliers were identified and 
prioritized for self-assessment surveys, and 156 on-site audits were conducted (excluding 
those who had already obtained RBA certification and those with audit scores of 80 or above 
in the previous year). All have completed sustainability risk assessments (with a 100% 
improvement response rate). Improvement measures were implemented and continuously 
monitored to ensure deficiencies were corrected, resulting in no suppliers being classified as 
non-complaint for violating responsible procurement standards.

Sustainability Assessment of New Suppliers
In 2024, a total of 578 new suppliers passed the selection process, with 78% of them returning 
the commitment letters. Since the Thailand plant was newly established, the signing process is 
ongoing. Additionally, 23 suppliers underwent on-site evaluations.
Implementation Standards
● Practice Regulations Comply with the "Supplier Social Responsibility and Ethical Code of 
Conduct Commitment Letter".
● Management Standards - All suppliers must agree with and sign the commitment.
Risk Rating
● Practice Regulations Proceed with risk grading according to the “Supplier Rating Mechanism”.
● Management Standards - High Risk, Medium Risk, Low Risk.
Onsite Audit
● Practice Regulations Conduct the onsite audit
● Management Standards - On-site audits are conducted with a score of 80 points or higher are 
considered qualified.
Risk Improvement and Follow-up
● Practice Regulations Social responsibility requirements of Compeq
● Management Standards - Issue audit reports and require improvements. If standards are not 
met, in addition to re-examination, include in the audit list for next year.
Sustainability Assessment of Existing Suppliers
For existing suppliers, they are categorized into three levels―high-, medium-, and low-risk levels 
based on procurement amount and supplier social responsibility risks (including social human 
rights, economic, and environmental aspects). Suppliers rated as low-risk need to verify whether 
they have signed the social responsibility commitment letter established by Compeq. Medium-risk 
suppliers, in addition to signing the commitment letter, must also complete a social responsibility 
self-assessment form for written review, and for those scoring above 80 points in the review are 
considered complaint. High-risk suppliers must not only sign the commitment letter and score 
above 80 points on the self-assessment form but also undergo on-site evaluations by Compeqs 
CSR Team.

2-7-2. Audit of Suppliers
We established the supplier audit standards according to SA8000 and RBA-CoC. For high-risk 
suppliers, we adopt the stage-based onsite audit at least once every three years. In 2024, we 
conducted onsite audits on 156 high-risk suppliers to ensure the sustainable operations of the 
supply chain.
In 2024, the audit coverage for high-risk suppliers reached 100%. All audits met the required 
standards, with an average audit score of 85.7. A total of 128 non-compliance items were 
identified, and corrective action plans (CAPs) were issued for all of them. Suppliers are required 
to meet Compeq’s improvement requirements within three months of the audit. This audit process 
ensures the effective implementation of sustainable practices in the supply chain. If suppliers fail 
to complete improvements within the deadline, the procurement unit will discuss and decide on 
actions such as reducing orders, reassigning orders, or terminating cooperation to ensure that risks 
are effectively controlled and reduced.
2-7-3. Contractors management
To protect the personnel of contractors and the employees of the Company and maintain plant 
safety, we have established the Contract HSE Management SOP according to the Occupational 
Safety and Health Act to specify the Company’s responsible unit, the responsibility of contractors, 
and the HSE matters for notice. Contractors must sign the contractor entry commitment documents 
(hazard notification form and toolbox meeting records) before applying for construction entry. They 
must also undergo hazard notification and safety and health education and training organized by the 
Industrial Safety Department. In 2024, a total of 1,816 contractors completed their training, totaling 
2,783 hours.
●	 Apart from requesting suppliers to propose corrective action, 
we will conduct a second audit as necessary to ensure 
all audited nonconformities are improved. In 2024, no 
supplier was disqualified for failure to make nonconformity 
improvements.
●	 27 of the key suppliers disclosed the corporate sustainability 
reports.
●	 20 key suppliers actively implemented the RBA VAP 
(accounting for 2.9% of all key suppliers and 6.7% of high-
risk key suppliers), of which 1 supplier had priority non-
conformities (5%) and 5 other non-conformities (25%), and 
95% have completed corrective actions for the deficiencies.
●	 A total of 25 key suppliers have conducted GHG inventory, 
of which 16 have obtained ISO 14064-1 certification, and 13 
of which have set carbon reduction targets.
●	 In green supply chain management, 14 utilize renewable 
energy, 3 participate in CDP disclosure, and 5 implement 
zero waste landfill management. Moving forward, 
continuous encouragement will be provided, and these 
factors will be incorporated as part of the supplier selection 
criteria.

2-7-4. Conflict Minerals Procurement Management
To achieve responsible and sustainable procurement, Compeq declares and 
commits to not directly or indirectly purchasing conflict minerals benefiting armed 
groups from the Democratic Republic of the Congo and neighboring regions. The 
Company rigorously implements due diligence to understand the source of minerals 
from suppliers, using the RMI’s conflict mineral investigation templates (CMRT, 
EMRT, AMRT) to assist in disclosing and communicating with smelters in the supply 
chain. Suppliers are required to disclose the source of minerals and comply with the 
policy of not using conflict minerals. To adhere to this policy, Compeq will:
●	 Conduct due diligence on the supply chain with respect to the “Due Diligence 
Guidance for Responsible Supply Chains of Minerals From Conflict-Affected and 
High Risk Areas” published by the OECD to ensure that products are free of the 
minerals from non-conflict-free smelters in Congo and its neighboring regions and 
abide by the RMI and international standards.
●	 Trace the sources of gold (Au), tantalum (Ta), tin (Sn), tungsten (W), cobalt (Co), 
mica, or other responsible minerals announced by the Responsible Minerals 
Initiative (RMI) in all products. All suppliers must complete the relevant due 
diligence surveys to confirm the source of these materials. Suppliers should use 
the RMI’s complaint smelters/refineries list to avoid directly or indirectly funding 
armed conflict groups or mineral regions that violate human rights.
●	 Continue to communicate this policy to suppliers and request them to 
communicate to their upstream and downstream suppliers, with the ultimate goal 
of facilitating smelters to participate in the conflict-free smelter program (CFSP). 
In 2024, no supplier was disqualified for violation.
In addition to publishing the above policies on the corporate website, we request 
suppliers to sign related statements to ensure no use of conflict minerals that will 
profit armed groups. Currently, the smelters supplying minerals are internationally 
recognized CFSs and meet international requirements. In view of the hierarchical 
supply chain relationship between the supply chain and mineral sources, before 
conducting due diligence, we first investigate the raw materials of the supply chain 
and define the applicable categories of conflict minerals in our products and identify 
suppliers requiring due diligence of conflict minerals. Through the top-down serial 
investigation of suppliers, we continuously follow up and adopt due diligence to 
minimize supply chain risk. If the mineral source country is the Democratic Republic 
of the Congo, an unusual management process must be initiated to develop a 
response plan. Suppliers are required to present a removal plan or improvement 
measures to ensure the legality of the conflict mineral source.

 2-8. Green Product Management
Compeq is committed to implementing green product management by establishing a Hazardous 
Substance Free (HSF) policy. This policy integrates the procurement, product, R&D, and 
manufacturing departments, ensuring that green materials are considered from the outset of 
production. The Company mandates that products must be free of substances harmful to human 
health and the environment, fulfilling the corporate responsibility to protect environmental and 
health safety. To ensure that Compeq reduces or prohibits substances within the specified 
timeframe and protects the environment while meeting customer needs, we have established 
a material restriction management system and management policies (HSF policy). This system 
covers the requirements of international regulations and customer demands, including RoHS, 
China RoHS, WEEE, REACH, and Halogen Free. We also engage third-party certification bodies 
for QC080000 certification to ensure the system’s effectiveness, ensuring that 100% of our products 
meet environmental label standards.
Comply with 
and educate

on HSF 
requirements

2-8-1. Toxic Substance Management of Supply Chain
Through the “Hazardous Substance Supplier Management System”, we effectively review if the 
raw materials or parts from suppliers meet the standards. We have also sorted out the limits of 
hazardous substances of individual customers by integrating part specifications, international 
laws and regulations, international directives, customer specifications, and supplier information 
and selected the lowest limit as the “Compeq Limit” for the incoming materials specifications. 
Additionally, we use the precision XRF incoming materials inspection instrument at plants to 
perform exact and stringent measurement and monitoring of restricted substances that impact and 
are hazardous to the environment. If there are changes or amendments to customer or international 
regulations, the Company will conduct an internal assessment, adjust control standards and 
operational procedures, ensure products meet customer requirements, and comply with relevant 
regulations and green product standards, to meet quality requirements and customer satisfaction.
In addition to abiding by the HSF requirements within the organization, we also request relevant 
suppliers to sign the “
Commitment to No Use of Prohibited/Restricted Substances Specified 
in Related Environmental Regulations ” to ensure that suppliers do not violate the regulations 
on restricted/limited substances (including, but not limited to the EU WEEE and RoHS) in the 
environmental protection regulations of any countries in production, manufacturing, packaging, 
storage, and transportation and continuously make effective control over raw materials and related 
materials to comply with green product standards and reduce the impact of product production on 
the natural environment to meet Compeq’s requirements on prohibited/restricted substances. In 
2024, we conducted HSF audits on 157 suppliers, and the passing rate of hazardous substance 
inspection was 100%.

Compeq is committed to reducing the use of hazardous substances by progressively integrating 
lead-free and halogen-free or low-halogen specifications into product materials and manufacturing 
processes. The goal is to achieve lead-free target by 2024. Regarding halogen usage, the target 
continues to be designed and produced according to customer requirements, with the introduction of 
halogens in new products managed and monitored according to Key Performance Indicators (KPIs).
2-8-2. Customer Health and Safety
Compeq products are printed circuit boards. Although the business model does not directly 
target and consumers, safety remains the top priority when developing new products. The 
products are UL certified to meet customer requirements, and regular factory inspections are 
conducted to ensure product quality. Certified products are guaranteed to be safe and 100% 
comply with the UL 94-V0 or 94-V1 flammability standards for plastic components in electronic 
products. Additionally, during the production of products and the procurement of raw materials, 
stringent control over the sourcing of supplier materials is maintained. The scope and standards 
of this control include HSF hazardous substances, REACH, and SVHC substances of very high 
concern. In 2024, there were no violations of relevant health and safety regulations or voluntary 
codes pertaining to products and services. We have established a comprehensive management 
system. The relevant green products and items that meet the standard regulations are as follows. 
(For detailed certificates, please visit https://www.compeq.com.tw/duty04.php?page=1.)

Material Topics and Major Responses of this Chapter
In response to the escalating issue of climate change, we formulated appropriate climate adaptation strategies to minimize operational impacts. The Company sets various environmental indicators, including 
GHG emissions, water usage, and waste management. We invested in process improvements to reduce environmental burdens at all stages of the product lifecycle. We also continue to advance management 
measures for climate change, energy management, water resources, and waste recycling, aiming to enhance resource efficiency and resilience in addressing sustainability issues.
Management Approach
Achievements in 2024
Accomplishment
Future Target
Climate change
●	 Follow the Task Force on Climate-related Financial 
Disclosure (TCFD) framework, including the four guiding 
principles of governance, strategy, risk management, 
and indicators and goals. Incorporate these principles 
into the risk management mechanism to identify physical 
and transition climate risks and opportunities, and make 
necessary operational adjustments to enhance climate 
resilience.
●	 In 2024, we obtained level B/B rating from CDP.
●	 Referencing IPCC and TCCIP climate scenario simulations, conduct an analysis of transition 
and physical risk impacts related to climate change for operational areas, using RCP2.6 and 
RCP8.5 scenarios. Analyze major disaster types of concern to stakeholders, such as high 
temperatures, droughts, typhoons, and other policy, regulations, and customer requirements. 
Develop impact adaptation plans for the short-, mid-, and long-term.
●	 Offset carbon emissions by 49.1% (216,309 metric tons of CO2e) with renewable energy use.
●	 More than 390 GWh of renewable energy was purchased; plants in China have installed solar 
panels for power generation, accounting for 33.1% of total energy consumption.
In progress
●	 Continuously reduce carbon emissions at the source 
(using low-carbon processes and fuels), manage energy 
targets, and implement energy-saving management 
plans for plant operations/processes.
●	 The goal is to increase the renewable energy usage 
ration to 30% by 2030. The Company is actively 
evaluating global markets to establish business 
partnerships for renewable energy, enhancing the 
sustainability and resilience of operations.
Energy Conservation and 
Emissions Reduction
●	 Actively implement various energy reduction measures 
and improve production technologies to optimize energy 
efficiency and thereby enhance energy efficiency.
●	 Replace energy-consuming equipment to reduce GMG 
emissions from the manufacturing process and meet the 
customer or government policy requirements.
●	 Each year we inventory GHG emissions and energy 
consumption according to ISO14064-1 to capture the 
current status to verify our reduction effectiveness. We 
also hire a third party to run external verification.
●	 In 2024, overall GHG emissions decreased by 3.2% CO2e compared to 2023, with emission 
intensity dropping by 13.4%. Scope 3 emissions totaled 204,699.7 metric tons of CO2e. The 
Company continues to strengthen supply chain management and collaborate to reduce GHG 
emissions.
●	 Taiwan and Huizhou (Plant and FPC Plant) completed the ISO 14064-1 inventory.
●	 In 2024, the total electricity consumption of the entire enterprise increased by 8.4% compared to 
2023, while the electricity consumption per unit of production value decreased by 3.6%.
●	 We implemented 171 energy-saving programs (41 for our plants in Taiwan and 130 for our 
plants in China), reducing electricity consumption by 43,957 MWh in total, equivalent to emitting 
24,379 metric tons of CO2.
In progress
●	 Implement energy conservation measures as per the 
governments net zero schedule, reduce emissions by 
30% over 2024 (base year) by 2030, and make rolling 
adjustments.
●	 Continue to focus on carbon reduction at the source, 
energy management, and energy-saving management 
plans to reduce GHG emission intensity by 1% per year.
Water Resource 
Management
●	 Enforce water management according to ISO 14001 
and enhance water efficiency through various water 
conservation and reclamation methods.
●	 The total enterprise-wide water consumption increased by 10.6% compared to 2023, with the 
water intensity per unit of output value decreased by 1.1%.
●	 The total wastewater discharge increased by 8.7% compared to 2023, and the wastewater 
discharge intensity decreased by 2.7%. We continued to promote a number of water-saving 
projects, and the total water recycling volume was 9.3%.
In progress
●	 Continuously implement the reasonable process water 
consumption program
●	 Water reclamation rate at 15%, and continuously reduce 
wastewater copper intensity to below 0.2mg/L.
●	 Optimize water source control and maintain no capacity 
loss due to water rationing.
●	 No significant leakage or spill and zero environmental 
grievance and fine in all plants.
Waste and 
Resource Efficiency
●	 Implement process technology improvements and source 
management measures to reduce waste production, 
recycle waste for reuse, and develop the circular economy 
through recycling.
●	 The total enterprise-wide waste generated increased by 2.5% compared to 2023, while the 
waste intensity per unit of output decreased by 8.3%.
●	 Proper waste disposal, landfilling rate of 0.02%, recycling rate of 89.5% and a waste conversion 
rate of 88.1% across Compeq businesses.
●	 Recycle and reuse sustainable materials (potassium gold cyanide 27.8%, waste copper 79.1%)
In progress
●	 Continuously implement waste reduction and raise the 
recycling rate to 90%.
●	 Maintain waste landfill at <1% moving toward zero 
landfill and continue to replace incineration and landfill 
with recycling, achieving a conversion rate of over 90%.
●	 Legal compliance for waste disposal, no significant fines, 
moving toward localization, waste to resources, and 
dispersion.

 3-1. Sustainable Environment Commitment and Policy
Climate Change and energy management are significant risk areas for Compeq’s sustainability. 
In addition to controlling emissions, air quality, water resources, and waste, the Company is 
committed to GHG adaptation and mitigation. To address climate change, we continuously 
analyze and manage internal energy use, referring to the Intergovernmental Panel on 
Climate Change (IPCC), Taiwan Climate Change Projection Information and Adaptation 
Knowledge Platform (TCCIP), industry trends, internal and external surveys, and corporate 
decisions. This involves identifying potential short-, mid-, and long-term operational risks 
due to climate change, and making adjustments through a PDCA cycle. Based on 2024 
data, the goal is to achieve a 30% reduction by 2030. Additionally, each plant is actively 
developing solutions (e.g.: energy-saving measures, establishing low-carbon energy 
sources, evaluating the use of low-carbon fuels, purchasing renewable energy etc.), to 
accelerate the achievement of carbon reduction goals. We are committed to providing the 
necessary resources to implement this policy:
●	 Maintain consistency with environmental safety legislation and the requirements of 
stakeholder groups of all business activities.
●	 Maintain continual improvement, prevent environmental pollution, and eliminate factors 
affecting the safety and health of stakeholders, hoping to minimize the impacts and 
hazards of our business activities.
●	 Implement green products and realize the non-use of environmentally sensitive 
substances during production.
●	 Provide reasonable time and resources for facilitating engagement in the ESH 
management system of stakeholders; enforce consultation and communication; and 
achieve the goals of environmental protection and occupational hazard prevention.
●	 Foster good neighbor relations, enhance corporate image, and achieve sustainable 
management goals.
 3-2. Climate Change Response
In response to the potential operational impacts of international carbon reduction trends, Compeq 
has conducted annual GHG inventory since 2009. Integrating local government requirements and our 
sustainability strategies, we work with CSR management systems, environmental engineering, safety 
and health centers, and relevant plant units to identify climate change risk based on daily operations. 
We assess significant climate risks and opportunities related to Compeq, develop and plan response 
measures, and actively build and strengthen mechanisms. Our strategies and actions for addressing 
climate change are formulated across key areas including “governance”, “strategy”, “risk management”, 
and “indicators and goals”, with the aim of mitigating the impact of climate risks.

3-2-1. Climate Change Governance
In alignment with the FSC’s sustainability roadmap, we report the status of GHG inventory to the Board of Directors every quarter, including updates on climate change-related initiatives and operational 
results, facilitating oversight and governance. A Sustainability Development Committee has been established, coordinated by the Chairman and Vice President who report to the Board of Directors. A 
Chief Sustainability Officer is appointed as the executive supervisor, overseeing five major functional units (Sustainable Operations and Risk Management, Sustainability Project Coordination, Compliance, 
Internal Audit, Finance and Accounting). The committee promotes climate change governance activities (technology, materials, plant affairs, energy use, and GHG inventory and reduction initiatives), 
low-carbon sustainable technologies (such as environmental engineering technology, environmental protection, procurement, R&D, and green electricity procurement and usage), sets climate change 
targets, risk control, and departmental collaboration. Internal meetings are held quarterly with the Chairman to report on climate change-related promotion plans and operational results for supervision and 
governance. Additionally, regular reports on the status of greenhouse gas inventories are presented to the Board of Directors.
Board of Directors level
✓ The highest management and decision-making body oversees the effective operation of the 
climate governance mechanism
Management Level
Formulate, promote, and strengthen the Company's climate change policies, annual plans, and 
strategies.
✓ Review, monitor, and amend the implementation status and effectiveness of climate change 
measures.
Climate Change Task Force
✓ The Sustainable Development Committee coordinates various units to 
identify climate-related risks and opportunities across all operational 
aspects, taking into account factors such as climate and environmental 
changes and shifts in international trends.

3-2-2. Risks and Opportunities due to Climate Change
●	 Compeq has adopted the TCFD assessment framework and, in reference to 
IPCC and TCCIP, conducted climate change scenario simulations. For the 
operational areas, impact analysis of climate change were carried out using 
RCP2.6 and RCP8.5 scenarios. The analysis focused on major disasters 
types of concern to stakeholders, such as high temperatures, droughts, and 
typhoons. Impact adaptation plans are being developed for the short-term 
(withing 3 years), mid-term (3 to 10 years), and long-term (over 10 years).
●	 Transition risk assessment: In the PCB industry, the financial impacts of the 
following factors on the supply chain's production processes are estimated, 
including the introduction of carbon fees in 2026, increases in water and 
electricity costs, energy efficiency requirements, various international carbon 
tax legislations and initiatives, total energy consumption management 
(including electricity, water, waste management, and GHG), changes in 
national energy policies, Renewable Energy Development Act and customer 
demand on renewable energy, and customer demands for renewable energy 
and low-carbon processes and fuels.
●	 Physical risk assessment: The main operational sites are assessed for risks 
associated with high temperatures and heavy rainfall, including water and 
electricity restrictions, power outages, typhoons, and floods.
●	 Opportunities for climate change: Regularly organize the replacement of 
high-efficiency processing equipment, implement equipment-plant energy-
saving operations, promote water-saving features in standby equipment, 
regularly review energy efficiency, continuously assess the use of renewable 
energy, and set internal carbon reduction targets and related reduction 
plans. Additionally, internal contingency plans for water and power shortages 
have been established to address these scenarios effectively.
●	 Implementation status: In response to stakeholders’ concerns about climate-
related risks and opportunities, and considering international trends, we 
incorporate relevant issues the Company is currently facing. Cross-departmental 
discussions identify short-, mid-, and long-term climate-related risks and 
opportunities. We analyze climate risks in our operations and across the industry 
supply chain, and develop relevant mitigation measures to effectively adapt to 
climate risks.
Note: RCP2.6 refers to low emissions (average temperature rise of 1.2°C), RCP8.5 refers 
to high emissions (average temperature rise of 3.0°C).

Compeq, referencing future climate model data from the Taiwan Climate Change Projection Information and Adaptation Knowledge Platform (TCCIP), conducted risks scenario simulations starting with the 
Taiwan plants. Future simulations will include the mainland China and Thailand plants, analyzing operational risks under RCP2.6 to RCP8.5 scenarios. This analysis will assess impacts on operations in the 
mid-century (2040 to 2060), considering factors such as increased temperatures, increased rainfall, and more days without rainfall.
RCP 2.6 and RCP 8.5 classify the extent of natural impact 
caused by extreme rainfall for the Taoyuan area

3-2-3. Climate Risk Management
In addressing climate risks issues, the Company follows the TCFD risk list, refers to CDP 
climate change and water questionnaires, and benchmarks against industry peers. The financial 
impacts and opportunities of climate change risks are managed according to the Company ’s 
risk management processes. The Company constantly use the PDCA management cycle to 
handle climate risk factors. Risks are assessed based on their likelihood and impact, including 
both physical and transition risks and opportunities. This involves identifying potential impacts 
from international climate change, industry trends, and key customer commitments to net-zero 
emissions (e.g., low-carbon and zero-carbon production requirements). The Company formulated 
response strategies to reduce the likelihood and extent of losses from these risks. After the 
assessment and analysis of likelihood and significance of impact, we focus on issues with medium 
and higher impact significance and draw up strategies, approaches, and countermeasures to 
address climate change, with the responsible departments planning the budget and implement the 
relevant tasks.
●   Identify potential risks and opportunities arising from policy, regulations, market, and 
technological changes, as well as reputation and material risks under different scenarios. 
Analyze these factors and determine their likelihood and impact using a matrix. Reassess 
physical risks, transition risks, and opportunities, and make iterative adjustments based 
on updates from IPCC and TCCIP.
●   For potential future operational threats, relevant departments will develop control 
measures to reduce the likelihood and impact of these risks on the Company.
Risk Management
Risk Management Process

opportunities

●	 Annually, identify the Companys

●	 In 2024, a total of 5 major

●	 Assess the likelihood, impact,

●	 Develop corresponding management

●	 Establish corresponding indicators 
and targets by responsible units 
to assess the implementation 
of relevant response strategies. 
Regularly report risk results and 
effectiveness to senior management 
and the Board of Directors for use in 
future operational decision-making 
and management

3-2-4. Climate Management Targets
Based on the latest international trends and the needs of stakeholders, we draw up climate change strategies and identify climate-related risks and opportunities. Through the periodic energy meetings, we 
implement the relevant policies and action plans and follow up on and manage performance through the PDCA cycle to reduce the impacts on the overall value chain due to climate change. Additionally, 
setting business continuity as the ultimate goal, we fortify plant operational facilities, enhance the capability of natural disaster regulation, set mitigation targets, and raise issue visibility through actions 
including energy management and water management to address the expectations of stakeholders.

 3-3. Greenhouse Gas Emission Management
Since 2009, Compeq has established the Company’s GHG emission inventory, gradually implementing management systems such as ISO 14001, ISO 14064-1 to promote GHG inventory operations. 
Following the ISO 14064-1 verification standards, an internal inventory mechanism was established to proactively conduct voluntary GHG emission inventory (for detailed certificates, please visit https://
www.compeq.com.tw/duty04.php?page=1). This process identifies carbon emission hotspots, allowing for analysis and the formulation of carbon reduction strategies. Currently, the Luzhu, Dayuan, Huizhou, 
and Huizhou FPC plants have obtained verification statements from third-party certifications. The Suzhou, Chongqing, and Thailand Plants conduct self-inventory and disclosure (with plans to complete 
third-party verification by 2027). The Company continuously invests in energy-saving projects and improvements in energy utilization to reduce the overall environmental impact.
Compeq is also actively monitoring the development of carbon emission trading to secure future carbon quotas. The Company participates in the Carbon Disclosure Project (CDP) questionnaire, which 
includes disclosures on GHG emissions, reduction targets and performance, and carbon issue management policies. Through this participation, Compeq utilizes the CDP evaluation results (B Level) as a 
guide for continuous improvement in carbon management.
Carbon Management Planning and Response
In response to international carbon pricing trends, Compeq continues to monitor global carbon market prices and GHG regulations, This information serves as a reference for carbon management 
and planning. Compeq proactively addresses issues related to the Renewable Energy Development Act, Climate Change Act (carbon tax), changes in electricity policies (electricity price increases), 
energy conservation goals and plans (1.5% energy reduction), carbon trading regulations, total energy consumption control (China’s 14th Five-Year Plan), the FSC’s net-zero carbon pathway, 
and regulatory requirements related to carbon emissions. By assessing the opportunities and risks associated with low-carbon transition, Compeq adjusted relevant policies and plans dynamically 
(including renewable energy procurement and solar panel installation at various sites, low-carbon assessments, boiler fuel at the Taiwan plant switched from diesel to natural gas, waste reduction 
and resource recovery initiatives).
The newly established Thailand plant is currently preparing to install a solar energy system. However, in terms of energy conservation, since it is presently in the trial production phase, energy-saving 
measures for equipment and plant operations will continue to be improved as mass production progresses. (New technology has already been implemented across the entire enterprise.)
