Methods and Results of GHG Inventory
The scope of GHG inventory includes the qualitative and quantitative inventory of 
Scope 1 direct GHG emissions and Scope 2 energy indirect emissions (GWP values 
are calculated using the IPCC-AR5 (Taiwan)/AR6 (China) versions). To identify key 
factors for climate change and mitigation, Compeq has extended carbon management 
to value chain partners by adopting ISO 14064-1: 2018 since 2021. In addition to its 
operational emissions, Compeq conducts Scope 3 category accounting and disclosure, 
and continues to collaborate with value chain partners to develop low-carbon products, 
collectively combating climate change and global warming.
In 2024, Compeq’s total GHG emissions (Scope 1+2) amounted to 440,799 metric tons of CO2e. The main 
source was the purchased electricity required for company operations, which accounted for 421,795 metric tons 
(95.7%) of the emissions. Emissions from fixed and mobile combustion sources in the production process (such 
as oil used in boilers, vehicles, and emergency generators), as well as process and fugitive emissions, accounted 
for 19,004 metric tons (4.3%). This indicates that 96% of the Company’s GHG emissions come from energy 
indirect emissions produced by purchased electricity, heat, and steam. To effectively reduce GHG emissions, 
reducing electricity usage is the most direct approach. Each plant is independently implementing measures 
to reduce energy consumption in the production process, improve equipment efficiency, and manage 
energy (details in 3-4 Energy Management). Additionally, Compeq actively promotes voluntary reductions 
and participates in the Industrial Development Bureau’s annual voluntary GHG reduction initiatives. We 
will continue to introduce energy-saving and carbon-reducing technologies, strengthen carbon emission 
management, and develop renewable energy projects (such as purchasing green electricity and installing 
solar panels) to streamline various energy uses and improve energy efficiency, thereby reducing GHG 
emissions.
Compeq aims to manage and reduce GHG emission intensity by 1% annually. In 2024, the total GHG 
emissions decreased by 14,731.1 metric tons of CO2e (3.2%) compared to 2023 (the base year), with 
emission intensity dropping by 13.4%. This reduction indicates improved manufacturing efficiency, which 
has led to decreased GHG emission intensity. Additionally, under internal energy management initiatives, 
the efficiency of utility systems and production processes has significantly improved. In the future, we will 
continue to reduce energy consumption at the source and adjust and optimize product structure to increase 
revenue growth momentum so as to accomplish the long-term target of consumption intensity reduction.
Note 1: In 2024, due to changes in the boundaries of the GHG inventory reports for 
each plant (with the addition of new Scope 3 inventory items) and the inclusion 
of the Thailand plant, the base year has been changed to 2024.
Note 2: Due to the environmental regulations on climate change by the Ministry of 
Environment, the Taiwan plant adopts the GWP value based on IPCC-AR5.

From the

Other Indirect Emissions
Since 2022, Compeq has incorporated Scope 3 emissions inventory (currently only for Luzhu/
Dayuan/Huizhou Plant/Huizhou FPC Plant). This involves evaluating other indirect emissions 
from outsourced activities, including those generated by other companies, incinerators, or 
landfills. Following third-party verification and disclosure, significant indirect emission sources 
are identified based on factors such as materiality, impact, data accessibility, and accuracy. 
Significant sources are included in the inventory scope, expanding carbon management to 
include value chain partners. In 2024, the total Scope 3 emissions were 204,699.7 CO2e. The 
findings help Compeq understand the energy use of downstream customer products and the 
emission contribution from various activities. Future efforts will focus on strengthening supply 
chain management through Scope 3 inventory, creating opportunities for collaboration with 
suppliers, and enhancing product energy efficiency to jointly reduce GHG emissions with 
upstream and downstream partners.
Types and Emissions of GHG
Compeq established a GHG emission inventory based on ISO 14064-1 and conducted annual 
GHG inventory. The types of GHG include carbon dioxide (CO2e), methane (CH4), Nitrous oxide 
(N2O), Hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs), Perfluorinated chemicals (PFCs), sulfur fluoride (SF6), and 
Nitrogen trifluoride (NF3). Compeq’s main GHG is CO2e. The main sources of emissions are 
electricity usage, septic tanks, and air conditioning refrigerants.

 3-4. Energy Management
To reduce energy consumption, Compeq has established an energy-saving and carbon-reduction plan that integrates strategies and solutions across various departments. The Company holds quarterly 
energy-saving meetings to review and track the effectiveness of implementation, continuously introducing energy-saving technologies and carrying out improvement plans for related facilities. In addition to 
implementing electricity-saving measures and enhancing energy efficiency, we also promote energy-saving initiatives in office and public areas to strengthen employees’ awareness and habits related to 
energy conservation and carbon reduction. In response to Taiwan’s regulations (which require at least 10% of corporate electricity use to come from green electricity) and customer demands, we use green 
electricity as a supplementary measure. We have also been evaluating the inclusion of Renewable Energy Certificates (RECs), Power Purchase Agreement (PPA), and carbon credits in our plants. The goal 
is to continue progressing toward 100% renewable energy use.
In 2024, the amount of renewable energy used through purchased green electricity certificates reached 396,896 MWh, accounting for 33.1% of the total electricity consumption. The total electricity 
consumption in 2024 was 1,197,673.0 MWh, representing an increase of 8.4% compared to 2023. In terms of electricity intensity per unit of output value, the overall electricity consumption per unit of output 
value in 2024 was 18.0, which is a decrease of 3.6% compared to 2023.

3-4-1. Energy Use Structure
Compeq’s main energy consumption consists of 71.7% purchased electricity for com operations, 26.1% of which is purchased renewable energy. Indirect energy is all purchased electricity, while direct 
energy usage includes fossil fuels such as diesel, gasoline, and natural gas, mainly used for emergency generators, forklifts, and company vehicles. In 2024, the total energy use was 4,449,184.0 GJ, a 
decrease of 13.0% compared to 2023. According to the GHG inventory analysis, purchased electricity is the largest source of GHG emissions at Compeq’s main production sites. Improving energy efficiency 
and increasing the renewable energy ratio are Compeq’s energy management policies.

From the

3-4-2. Energy Conservation
To continuously saving energy, we implemented reduction through the following two main 
pathways: efficiency enhancement and equipment replacement in 2024. To ensure the 
implementation of energy management and energy conservation projects, we establish a 
responsible energy unit in each plant. Apart from holding the energy management meeting each 
quarter to review the energy status and progress of project implementation of the plant, all plants 
share the achievements and experience in project implementation and continuously implement 
improvement measures including replacing traditional lighting fixtures with energy-efficient 
lighting, compressor systems, and aircon equipment and energy-conservation equipment. We also 
combined the proposal reward policy to continuously reduce energy and electricity consumption, 
which continued the direction of our energy conservation policy. In 2024, a total of 171 energy-
saving projects were implemented (41 in Taiwan plants and 130 in Mainland China plants), 
resulting in a total energy saving of 43,957.0 MWh. This is equivalent to a reduction of 24,379.0 
metric tons of CO2e emissions, with improved carbon reduction performance of 134.3% compared 
to the previous year.
 3-5. Air Pollution Management
Compeq prioritizes the working environment and air pollution control for its employees. According to 
internal procedures, gases are collected through pipes after emission and are treated by exhaust gas 
treatment equipment before being discharged. High-efficiency control and treatment equipment (such 
as exhaust gas scrubbers, dust collectors, and exhaust gas ducting with added sodium thiosulfate 
control) are used to process the exhaust gases, reducing the pollutants entering the atmosphere. The 
pollutant content is maintained in accordance with (or below) government environmental regulations, 
and all plants have obtained pollution discharge permits issues by the government.
Due to the different processes of each factory, the air pollutants produced are different. The main 
focus is to continuously monitor and control nitrogen oxides (NOx), sulfur oxides (SOx), and volatile 
organic compounds (VOCs). Each plant conducts regular self-assessments and hires external 
professional agencies for testing to ensure compliance with local government environmental 
regulations. Additionally, in response to operational conditions and local environmental policies, 
measures such as replacing diesel with heat pumps, switching from heavy oil boilers to diesel boilers, 
and using low-VOCs emission cleaning products are implemented. These practices aim to reduce 
VOCs pollutants at the source and during discharge treatment. Continuous updates to air pollution 
control equipment are carried out to monitor, control, and optimize the exhaust gas treatment 
process, effectively reducing VOCs consumption. The use of ozone-depleting substances (ODS) 
such as CFC-11 (trichlorofluoromethane) is not employed.

To maintain optimal equipment performance, each piece of equipment undergoes regular 
maintenance and inspections. In the event of an emergency, backup equipment should be 
immediately available, and there are emergency power systems in place. The system parameters are 
continuously monitored, and operators receive comprehensive training. If deviations beyond preset 
limits are detected alerts will be promptly issued, allowing immediate action to ensure the system 
operates normally and that emitted gases do not pose a threat to the surrounding environment.

 3-6. Water Resource Management
3-6-1. Water Intake Structure
Our production bases are all located in Taiwan, mainland China, and Thailand. As rainfall 
distribution is uneven by region and by season, regional or seasonal droughts are common. As 
a result, water management is essential to our operations. Therefore, we continuously enhance 
water efficiency based on the “reduce--> recycle --> reuse” model. The water source is 100% tap 
water. Water is mainly consumed by domestic use and plant peripheral equipment. Additionally, 
as no business location is located in or adjacent to protected areas, and not water is withdrawn 
from protected areas or water source areas, our operational activities will not bring significant 
environmental impacts to water sources and local ecosystems and environments.
Compeq follows the TCFD framework and utilizes the WRI Aqueduct water resource scenario 
simulation tool to analyze geographical locations and assess the risk level of water resources. This 
approach helps in proactively managing water resources and setting up water recycling facilities. 
The Company continuously promotes water-saving measures and is committed to water recycling 
and reuse to enhance adaptive capacity. In 2024, no operational incidents related to water usage 
occurred.
3-6-2. Water Consumption
In 2024, Compeqs total water usage was 11,759.2 thousand cubic meters (m³), a decrease of 
1,122.4 thousand cubic meters (10.6%) compared to 2023. The water intensity for 2024 was 
0.2 per unit of output, showing no significant change from 2023. Moving forward, the Company 
will continue to focus on water conservation, improve BOM water management, and enhance 
water recycling and reuse to improve water efficiency, with an ongoing target of reducing water 
consumption by 1%.

3-6-3. Water Recycling and Water-Saving Measures
As the PCB manufacturing process consumes a large amount of water, each plant has 
established a responsible water management unit to plan, establish, implement, monitor, and 
analyze water consumption, eliminate anomalies, and make continual improvements. Apart from 
actively considering and assessing the increase in water reclamation for reuse, we emphasize 
water consumption reduction and water recycling and reuse. Prioritize the use of water-saving 
equipment. Wastewater, after treatment, is recycled according to the water quality requirements 
of various usage points for reuse in production, environmental cleaning, and other processes. In 
2024, multiple water-saving projects were implemented, such as process rationalization water 
management plans, process optimization improvements, and the establishment of a water usage 
auditing system, to enhance water recycling. The total recycled water volume in 2024 was 882.5 
thousand cubic meters, with a recycling rate of 7.5%.
3-6-4. Wastewater Management
In 2024, Compeq ’s total wastewater discharge was 9,525.6 thousand cubic meters, an 8.7% 
increase compared to 2023. The wastewater discharge intensity increased by 2.7%.To ensure 
compliance with regulatory discharge standards, Compeq implements an ISO 14001 environmental 
management system to systematically manage environmental issues. The wastewater generated 
at the plants is treated appropriately or legally discharged into designated sewage areas. The 
Plants in Taiwan Huizhou and Thailand plants have dedicated wastewater treatment facilities. In 
Chongqing and Suzhou Plant, which are located in industrial parks, wastewater water is treated 
through centralized treatment systems. All production and domestic wastewater are collected 
separately, and routine sampling and third-party quality checks are conducted. Wastewater 
quality at all plants meets local discharge standards, ensuring minimal environmental impact on 
surrounding water bodies. In 2024, there were no significant leakage or overflow incidents, and no 
environmental complaints or penalties were reported.

Additionally, in response to the tightening effluent heavy metal control standards in Taiwan, 
the Luzhu and Dayuan plants continuously implement the heavy metal reduction plan. In 2024, 
apart from continuously optimizing and adjusting the electrolysis copper reclamation system and 
completing the ion exchange resin tower of all plants to reduce the copper content in wastewater, 
we also devoted to reducing and reclaiming copper in wastewater. In the future, in addition to 
legal compliance, we will manage the copper content in effluents with stricter regulations to 
reduce the load of receiving water and continuously assess the enhancement of the overall 
treatment performance through equipment adjustment and modification, such as adding electrolytic 
equipment to enhance copper removal capability and to ensure more stable wastewater operation.

 3-7. Waste Management
At Compeq, the waste generated from production is classified into two categories by law: 
hazardous and non-hazardous. We establish a responsible unit according to the ISO14001 EMS to 
effectively capture the waste output at its sources. Based on the concept of minimization of waste 
generation and maximization of waste recycling, we select qualified contractors that can effectively 
dispose of waste to make proper waste disposal. We also audit waste disposal contractors from 
time to time for lawful waste disposal to ensure waste is properly disposed of or recycled. Waste 
within the business is disposed of domestically and no transnational waste disposal is practiced. All 
hazardous industrial waste generated is disposed of domestically by qualified contractors.
Waste is processed with the priority to recycle. For example: Heavy metal waste mud produced 
by water processing plant is categorized as corporate waste in accordance with legislation and 
therefore should be processed by licensed waste disposal and processing contractor. However, 
through the promotion of the recycling system, the volume of waste mud has been reduced 
significantly. Additionally, for important wastewater and waste liquid containers, secondary 
cofferdams and liquid breakers are equipped to prevent leakage.
As scrapped PCBs are also waste, we also outsource their disposal. Currently, we are developing 
effective recycling technology to turn waste into resources to reduce waste generation. 
Additionally, we continue to value waste to resources and nontoxic disposal of waste and proceed 
with waste disposal strictly according to the law in terms of three goals: localization, dispersion, and 
waste to resource.
3-7-1. Structure of Waste Production and Disposal
In 2024, Compeq generated a total of 76,502.2 metric tons of waste, with general waste accounted 
for 31.9% and hazardous waste for 68.1%. This represents an increase of 1,850.3 metric tons 
(2.5%) compared to 2023. Specifically, general waste increased by 4,864.1 metric tons (24.9%), 
and hazardous waste decreased by 3,013.8 metric tons (5.5%). The waste intensity continues to 
show a downward trend, decreasing by 8.3% compared to 2023. The Company will continue to 
focus on source reduction and in-house waste recycling and reuse. Notably, 89.5% of the waste 
is processed by recycling vendors and reused as industrial raw materials (e.g., converting copper 
sludge into electrolytic copper pipes). Future efforts will include ongoing waste reduction and 
increasing recycling rates, such as dismantling non-combustible waste, reusing filter cartridges, 
and optimizing copper pipe recycling, to achieve sustainable development goals for effective waste 
reuse. Additionally, as we are not an end-product manufacturer, we cannot trace the disposal 
method and recycling status of products at the end of life (EOL). Hence, related data cannot be 
quantified.

3-7-2. Waste Reduction Measures and Benefits
Compeq not only implements source reduction but also enhances process design and technology 
to reduce raw material consumption. This is carried out in compliance with international trends in 
waste reduction, simultaneously executing waste reuse, reduction plans, and recycling. The Company 
aims to advance toward localization, resource utilization, and decentralization goals. This approach 
aligns with international trends in waste reduction and lowers operational costs by decreasing waste 
treatment expenses. Additionally, the Company aims to transform waste into valuable resources, 
yielding three main benefits of waste reduction, reduced energy and cost for waste treatment, and 
revenue from recycling and regenerating resources. The Company conducts specialized reviews 
for precious metal usage and recovery (e.g., projects for recovering gold from membrane waste 
liquids, aging liquids, gold resin processes, gold-dusted materials, gold stripping methods, and other 
gold-containing resin recoveries). By prioritizing reduction targets for major waste-contributing raw 
materials, we evaluated feasible solutions through small-scale trials. Upon successful verification, 
these solutions are expanded across plants to achieve waste reuse, reduction, and recycling, 
progressing towards local resource-efficient, and decentralized goals.
Circular Use of Materials
In addition to reduction at the source, we further promote recycling and reuse to turn waste into 
recycled resources so as to reduce waste, reduce energy consumption and cost for waste disposal, 
and create benefits from waste recycling. If the PCB manufacturing process uses potassium gold 
cyanide as one of the materials, the discharged aging solution and gold stripping solution will be 
recycled and refined by the potassium gold cyanide supplier, and then provided back to Compeq for 
reuse, achieving sustainable material utilization.
2024 Reduction Results
Total waste reduction: 5,602.7 metric tons
Waste reduction benefit: NTD 39.06 million
● Continue to recover copper and turn copper sludge 
into electrolytic copper tubes
● Domestic/production waste reduction
● Drying and weight reduction of dry film residue
● Reduction of filter cartridges

3-7-3. Direction of Future Promotion
 3-8. Environmental Management and Legal Compliance
In line with international environmental issues and trends, Compeq has progressively 
implemented ISO 14001 and ISO 14064-1 management systems across its main plants. This 
ensures compliance with local government environmental regulations while pursuing operational 
performance. Regular Environmental, Safety, and Health (ESH) review meetings are held to 
evaluate the previous years ESH management plans, goals, and their execution. Concurrently, 
new ESH management goals for the current year are established and implemented by the relevant 
departments.
3-8-1. Compliance with Environmental Regulations
We treat legal compliance as a basic requirement. We also set up a stakeholder section on the 
corporate website. After receiving any issues or complaints relating to environmental protection, 
we will handle and address them according to the internal SOPs. In 2024, there were no production 
halt or plant demonstration by local residents due to pollution or leakage of any kind was reported.
3-8-2. Expenditures on Environmental Protection
With a focus on sustainable operations, Compeq not only acquires certifications for environmental 
management systems but also adopts various environmental protection measures, investing 
annually in pollution prevention, energy conservation, waste management, and management 
system certifications. The Company emphasizes circular economy principles and enhances in-
plant resource reuse by introducing energy-efficient equipment to improve recycling efficiency. 
In addition to collaborating with government environmental agencies to establish environmental 
monitoring systems, we also comply with international customer requirements by implementing 
preventive and corrective measures to address climate change, gradually increasing investment 
in environmental protection equipment each year. In 2024, a total of NTD 1,007,263 thousand was 
invested in environmental protection, an increase of 30.1% compared to 2023.

Material Topics and Major Responses of this Chapter
As a people-oriented business, we are committed to building a friendly workplace environment where the right people can work in the right place without worries to enhance the sense of work security and 
happiness. Particularly, we put the OH&S of employees first by shaping a safety-first corporate culture, identifying potential industrial safety risks, and building a worry-free workplace environment. Through 
the transparent and unfettered labor-management communication mechanism, we protect the rights, interests, and workplace safety of employees to realize total participation.

Human
Rights 
Commitment
 4-1. Human Rights Protection and Maintenance
Employees are one of our most important assets. In addition to strictly abiding by various labor laws 
and regulations, we also comply with stricter standards for labor, health and safety, environment, 
ethics, and management systems, such as international and customer codes of conduct to build 
a healthy and safe workplace environment for the right people to work in the right place. We also 
offer a complete and generous remuneration and benefit system, care about the physical and 
mental health of employees, and plan a complete talents development system to help employees 
demonstrate their specialty at work.
Compeq also regards occupational safety and health as fundamental requirements. By fostering 
practical safety measures, identifying potential safety risks, and establishing transparent and 
effective labor-management communication mechanisms, the Company protects employee rights 
and workplace safety. Additionally, we have proactively applied for SA8000 Social Accountability 
certification. Currently, the certifications have been obtained for the Luzhu, Dayuan, Huizhou 
(Huizhou Plant and Huizhou FPC Plant), and Chongqing Plant. We are also applying to join the 
RBA-On platform and gradually advancing towards RBA audit certification to ensure a consistent 
work structure and adherence to standards in managing human rights issues. Annual self-
assessments confirm that in 2023, there were no significant human rights violations at any site, 
with no forced labor or coercion of unwilling personnel.
4-1-1. Human Rights Commitment and Policy
Compeq supports and adheres to international guidelines such as the United Nations Global 
Compact (UNGC), the Universal Declaration of Human Rights,and the ILO Declaration on 
Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work, and has established a human rights policy 
accordingly. We ensure no discrimination against employees based on race, gender, age, political 
party, religion, or disability. Employing employees not only complies with local minimum age 
regulations, local laws, and RBA-related requirements but also mandates that all employees 
adhere to relevant regulations in their daily work and business activities.
Every year we review whether or not the internal system complies with the latest RBA standards 
to enforce the requirements of RBA-CoC. In terms of human rights issues, we identify the potential 
risks and issues of human rights violation in each plant through self-assessment and employee 
interview, find defects based on the risk assessment results and through internal and external 
audits, and implement human rights protection, damage mitigation programs, or compensation 
measures.
In addition to internal self-assessment mechanisms, we also respond to customers request 
by having third-party organizations conduct RBA verification audits (VAP). This external audit 
perspective enhances the overall management system. The audit reports are transparently shared 
with clients through the RBA-ON system. The validity period of these audits is two years. The 2024 
RBA Self-Assessment Questionnaire (SAQ) results all indicate a low risk level.

Promotion of Human Rights Management and Mitigation Measures
Compeq incorporates human rights considerations into all aspects of its operations by using SA8000 and RBA standards for human rights risk assessment. The Company conducts internal audits through 
self-checks, HR internal reviews, and employee interviews to regularly assess human rights risk exposure. Additionally, we perform human rights surveys and on-site audits of external value chain partners, 
implementing corrective measures as needed. Throughout the Company, we have conducted 8 internal assessments and undergone 25 external audits, taking various mitigation and improvement actions 
based on audit results.

Human Rights Performance
Compeq complies with all relevant local labor laws and industry benchmark regulations, formulating 
human rights mitigation or compensation measures. The Company also reduces the risk of human 
rights violations among suppliers through advocacy, self-assessment forms, or on-site audits. In 
2024, there were no significant human rights violations. The control over overtime working hours 
continued to be effectively implemented and alleviated, with continuous improvements. Regarding 
the other human rights risks mentioned above, which are not classified as high risk, we regularly 
review our human rights control mechanisms, continuously implementing three major mitigation 
measures of education and training, advocacy and communication, and system management. We 
evaluate the effectiveness of these measures and provide due diligence reports to the management 
team to minimize human rights impacts.
Human Rights-Related Training
We sign an employment contract with every employee out of his/her free will. In 2024, there was no 
forced labor, coercion, and discrimination. Every year we arrange training and outreach in relation 
to human rights protection for new employees and in-service employees through e-learning, 
memos, communication channels, posters, CSR cards, and meetings. The aforementioned 
courses are mandatory for all employees. In 2024, human rights protection training totaled 
19,000 participant, with over 39,000 total training hours. All employees completed the human 
rights training, and Compeq will continue to promote related education and training to enhance 
awareness of human rights protection.

From the

Preventive Measures for Workplace Violence
We have established the “Anti-Workplace Violence Policy” to proactively build a friendly workplace 
environment, strictly inhibit workplace bullying by management, and maintain zero tolerance 
against violence, either physical or mental, among employees or on Compeq employees by visitors, 
customers, or strangers to demonstrate our determination for “zero tolerance” against workplace 
violence. We have also established the “Regulations for Prevention, Correction, Complaint, and 
Punishment of Sexual Harassment at Workplace” to realize workplace gender equality. We have 
also set up hotlines and email for sexual harassment grievances. Apart from keeping the identity 
of complainants confidential to protect their rights and interests, we also help victims of workplace 
violence and sexual harassment file grievances or take subsequent legal actions so as to build a 
friendly and safe workplace environment. In 2024, there was no confirmed workplace violence and 
sexual harassment.
Additionally, for each employee to understand workplace sexual harassment and know how to deal 
with it and where to seek assistance, we arrange recurrent training periodically over the in-house 
e-learning platform. We also include this as a compulsory of new employees for employees to 
understand more about sexual harassment and so to protect their rights and interests.
4-1-2. Gender Equality and Care
Compeq grants employees the right to take unpaid parental leave in accordance with regulations. For 
employees who need to breastfeed or express milk for children under 2 years old, in addition to the 
mandated breaks, an additional one hour of paid breastfeeding time is provided each day. We also offer 
special meals for pregnant employees, designated parking spaces for pregnant employees, and a warm 
and comfortable breastfeeding environment with dedicated mothers rooms.
The reinstatement rate following parental leave in 2024 was 76.0%, and the retention rate 
was approximately 96.6%. We continue to provide smooth channels for unpaid parental leave, 
enabling employees to balance family and career while promoting gender equality, ensuring 
better protection for both male and female employees. We proactively inquire about employees’ 
willingness to return to work before the end of their leave and offer birth subsidy of NTD 2,000 per 
child, provided by the Welfare Committee. Additionally, we continuously observed the work status 
of employees after their return from parental leave. Employees who did not return to work after 
parental leave chose voluntary resignation because they still needed to take care of their family 
after the expiration of the unpaid parental leave.

Zero 
tolerance
We maintain zero tolerance against violence, either physical or mental, among employees or on 
Compeq employees by visitors, customers, or strangers.
Remedies include absolute confidentiality of identity, assistance for a job content adjustment or 
position change, physical and mental health follow-up.
Workplace bullying (violence) should be reported immediately through the employee grievance 
hotlines or grievance email. maibox@compeq.com.tw/-03 3231111#2230、2210
Include workplace bullying (violence) as a required course for new employees and all 
employees, and arrange recurrent training every year.
The grievance investigation team will confidentially investigate the matter for the grievance 
review committee to make the resolution. If a workplace bullying grievance is verified, the related 
parties will be disciplined in accordance with the discipline regulations.

From the

To provide female employees with a worry-free working environment, priority parking spaces 
and maternity meals are offered to pregnant employees. Additionally, lactation rooms and 
"Dedicated Mother’s Rooms" (Mainland China) are established to provide a quiet and comfortable 
environment for milk expression. These facilities are equipped with dedicated lockers, refrigerators, 
and water heaters. Employees may use these facilities outside of designated break times, and 
breastfeeding time is considered working hours without any adverse impact on salary. The 
infirmary also assesses maternity health hazards for pregnant and breastfeeding employees. In 
2024, a total of 253 employees received an assessment by the plant physicians. Additionally, the 
Mainland China plants consider the needs and concerns of pregnant employees, allowing them to 
opt for manual security checks to avoid passing through security gates, thereby demonstrating care 
and respect for pregnant employees.
The Company also abides by the Occupational Safety and Health Act to adopt hazard 
assessments, control, and grade management for jobs with threats of maternity health hazards. For 
female employees who are pregnant or within one year after delivery, we adopt health protection 
measures, including duty adjustment or replacement according to the adaptive assessment and 
recommendations given by the plant physicians and maintain relevant records. Additionally, we 
provide employees with health education information, hold maternity health talks regularly, and 
provide childcare consultation services for pregnant employees through the plant nurses.
4-1-3. Migrant Worker Concerns and Care
In response to labor demands, Taiwan plants hire foreign migrant workers. The hiring process and 
management adhere to international human rights and RBA regulations. The Company fully covers 
the relevant expenses incurred before the foreign employees ’ employment and conducts due 
diligence on domestic and international agencies to ensure compliant hiring practices.
In 2023, following the COVID-19 pandemic, Compeq continued to monitor disease information both 
abroad and domestically, including preventive information on diseases such as dengue fever and 
monkeypox. Regular cleaning and disinfection of living areas were conducted to ensure a high 
quality of living environment. The average tenue of foreign employees was 3.1 years, with 244 of 
them having been employed for over 5 years.
Matter for Notice of 
Migrant Workers
Related Practice
Human Rights Management
Migrant Worker 
Human Rights 
Management
● New migrant workers are issued RBA and relevant company policy promotion 
handbooks, and different administrators and Line groups are created according

●	 Exclusive breastfeeding room for mothers to breastfeed more comfortably with better privacy and 
convenience.
●	 Exclusive pink vest for pregnant women to prevent collisions and move with confidence.
To acknowledge the significant contributions of female employees to both the Company and their 
families, each plant expresses respect and appreciation through various means (e.g., flower-giving 
activities on International Women’s Day) to specifically thank women for their contributions in the 
workplace.

 4-2. Employee Overview and Distribution
With our global expansion strategy, our workforce continues to grow. As of the end of 2024, the total number of employees across the Company is 21,927, an increase of 165 (0.8%) compared to the previous 
year. The Company remains steadily developed and is preparing talent in advance to meet competitive challenges due to overseas expansion plans. Among the employees, the largest number is in the 
Huizhou Plants in China (Huizhou and Huizhou FPC Plants), accounting for approximately 50.2% of the total workforce, followed by the Luzhu Plant in Taiwan, which represents about 21.6% of the total. 
Foreign employees in Taiwan accounted for about 20.2% of the formal staff, including a diverse range from the Philippines, Indonesia, and Thailand. At the Thailand plant, employees of Myanmar nationality 
account for approximately 27.0%. Additionally, there were no part-time employees hired in 2024; 100% of the workforce are full-time employees. Based on the relevant CSR standards, we do not restrict or 
force employees, nor do we force, jail, or bond labor in any form or withhold the ID cards, passports, and alien resident certificates, or money of migrant workers. All employees must work voluntarily.
In accordance with SA8000 and RBA standards, and important customers requirements, we strictly prohibit the use of child labor. To prevent the inadvertent use of child labor, we have established a 
comprehensive child labor remediation management procedure. This includes rigorous recruitment screening and procedures for addressing any inadvertent use, such as providing necessary educational 
support and assisting with the payment of related educational expenses to ensure that any inadvertently employed children can continue to receive compulsory education.
Most employees of plants in Taiwan are 30-
50 years old, accounting for about 62.4% 
of the total. Most employees of plants in 
mainland China are mostly under 30 years 
old, accounting for over 40.1%, suggesting 
that both employees and job applicants in 
mainland China are younger.
As the PCB manufacturing process still 
relies on manual and physically demanding 
work, the percentage of male employees 
(60.5%) is higher than that of female 
employees (39.5%).

 4-3. Talents Employment and Retention
New Employees Overview
Compeq abides by local labor laws and regulations and strictly identifies the actual age of employees in recruitment to avoid unintended use and hiring of child labor. We also ensure no worker aged under 18 
engages in dangerous or hazardous jobs and provide appropriate protection for pregnant employees. As we are in a technology- and labor-intensive industry, we need a great deal of on-site operation work, 
with male employees being the major workforce. Therefore, we have a higher proportion of male employees than female employees. If analyzed by age group, the number of employees under 30 increased 
the most.

From the 
Chairman
Employee Turnover
The number of employees who left the Company in 2024 increased by about 6.5% compared to the number in 2023, primarily due to a higher turnover rate among direct employees in the Mainland China. 
This was a result of product structure adjustments and workforce reorganization, focusing on retaining stronger personnel and allocating resources to more stable business units. In terms of age group, the 
largest number of employees resigned were those under 30 years old. Feedback on the reasons for leaving indicates issues such as poor job fit and incorrect perceptions of job conditions and environment 
(e.g., not being aware of the need for long periods of standing or wearing cleanroom suits). To address these issues, improvements have been made in the recruitment process and onboarding training, such 
as site visits during interviews and adaptation interviews after three months for new recruits. Through the mentoring system and resignation process improvement, supervisors and HR personnel interview 
resigned employees to understand their reasons for resignation. Additionally, through personal specialties, job content, and workplace adjustment or offering opportunities for internal transfer, we achieved 
the goal of employee retention to actively offer potential return of employees with the opportunities for returning to work.
Note: Turnover rate = total number of employees resigned in the year (resigned in 2024)/number of 
employees in each age group at the end of 2024 (2024/12/31)/12 months. Voluntary turnover rate 
includes those who actively submit their resignation. Overall turnover rate includes both voluntary 
turnover (including retirement) and involuntary turnover (including dismissals, layoffs, and deaths).

From the

Employment of Local Management Personnel
Local employment has always been our major principle to fully create job opportunities for residents in 
local communities. Therefore, apart from prioritizing local residents in recruitment, we actively develop 
them into outstanding management staff. In 2024, most management staff in all Compeq plants were 
local employees. In Taiwan, all management staff are Taiwanese. Due to the complexity in employee 
turnover, plants in mainland China hire 47.0% of local employees on average. In Thailand, where 
a new plant is under construction, most senior executives are currently supported by Taiwanese 
personnel. In the future, we will actively practice localization to continuously increase local job 
opportunities.
Employee Diversity
Compeq is also committed to supporting the employment of underprivileged groups with physical and 
mental disabilities by providing appropriate job positions to enhance their employment opportunities 
and create a friendly workplace. Currently, all Taiwan-based facilities complies with the statutory 
employment standards and exceeds the employment quota by 125%. In the future, we will continue to 
actively evaluate job positions internally to exceed the required quotas and provide more employment 
opportunities for individuals with disabilities. Employees with disabilities account for 1.5% of the total 
workforce across the Company.
Compeq also respect unique culture of ethnic minorities. In Taiwan, we mainly employ indigenous 
people and grant 8 hours of ceremonial leave annually to employees with indigenous status. Overall, 
indigenous employees account for 4.0% of the workforce.
We maintain gender equality in the right to work and concern ourselves with the promotion 
and development of female employees. Due to the characteristics and labor source of the 
PCB employees, however, most management staff and line workers are male. In the future, 
we will consider the progressive increase in female supervisors.

From the

 4-4. Competitive Remuneration and Benefits
Compeq has established a remuneration system that ensures external competitiveness and 
internal fairness. Salaries are determined based on education, work experience, job position, 
performance, and market conditions. We ensure that starting salaries are not influenced by factors 
such as race, ethnicity, social origin, social class, ancestry, religion, physical disability, gender, 
sexual orientation, marital status, union membership, political views, age, or any other factors. 
We are performance oriented to plan fair, complete, and comprehensive salary and benefits to 
ensure the accomplishment of performance KPIs of all employees and departments and attract 
and retain talents. Apart from referring to the salary survey, living standard, CPI, minimum wage, 
and social welfare regulations of each location and determining remuneration by performance after 
acceptance, we also sign up to the TPCA salary survey every year. In addition to the base salary, 
we also adjust the employee salary according to the Company’s business performance and the 
industry standard to ensure the overall pay is competitive in the market.
●	 We comply with related local laws and regulations and align the starting salary standards for new 
graduates and foreign workers with the laws and regulations.
●	 We adjust salary every year based on the earnings in the year and the market salary survey.
●	 We issue performance bonuses according to operational performance and personal performance 
and set the amount according to each employee's duty, contribution, and performance.
●	 No differential treatment based on gender, race, religion, political affiliation, marital status, or 
union membership.
●	 We plan promotion each year according to employees' performance and developmental potential, 
organizational needs, employee adaptability, and career development intent.
Salaries of Non-management Full-time Employees in the Taiwan Plants
Non-management personnel refers to employees excluding directors and managers. In 2024, the 
average and median salaries form non-management employees increased compared to 2023.

From the

Well-structured Promotion System
A well-structured promotion and transfer system is used as an incentive to reduce employee 
turnover. The Company established a competitive salary system in the job market to retain talent, 
rewarding outstanding employees based on operational results and individual performance, 
thereby boosting morale and enhancing efficiency.
Supervisors guide employees in setting work goals to achieve the organization’s mid- and long-
term goals. They provide performance communication channels and conduct regular performance 
reviews and improvement discussions (monthly, semi-annually, and annually). In 2024, 100% of 
formal employees, regardless of gender or position, received evaluations. These evaluations are 
conducted fairly and objectively to assess employee performance, serve as a reference for talent 
development and personnel changes, and form the basis for promotions and salary adjustments. 
In addition, during the probation period of new employees, a new employee evaluation mechanism 
is established to ensure early confirmation of the suitability of new employees through personal 
feedback and supervisor evaluation results.
If an employee is not fit for the current job or the performance is behind the target, we will provide 
guidance and improvement plans or assistance for a job transfer. If an employee is still unable to 
cooperate with other employees, we will provide appropriate notification and redundancy pay by 
law and related certification of service to help apply for unemployment compensation and other 
assistance and thereby protect their rights and interests.
 4-5. Employee Development and Training
Professional talent development is a key asset for Compeq to face various challenges. We are 
committed to creating a rich and high-quality human resource pool through specialized training 
techniques and methods. We offer a series of comprehensive training programs, categorized 
by different fields according to the organizational structure (such as R&D, sales, production, 
quality control, finance, management, etc.). The highest management in each functional area are 
responsible for defining the required skills and knowledge for each position within that field and for 
nurturing their subordinates.
Every year the education planning unit investigates the training needs across the enterprise, 
analyze the competencies required by supervisors and employees, and establishes the annual 
training plan. In addition to building a complete training system and training courses, it also arranges 
training courses in different areas to match the Company’s strategies and annual directions to build an 
environment for continual learning and career growth.
Performance management not only evaluates colleagues’ achievement of goals but also integrates 
core competencies assessment to strengthen company culture. This includes evaluations of 
management and professional competencies to understand talent capabilities and identify gaps, 
with a focus on the long-term and future development of employees’ abilities.
●	 Planning corporate 
operational strategies 
and communication with

From the

In terms of the allocation of training resources, there is no gender or age difference. All employees, whether they are new recruits, foreign workers or dispatched workers, must undergo pre-employment 
training. For current employees, we offer both online and in-person training courses. The training methods are diverse, including classroom lectures, seminars, group meetings, bulletin boards, and weekly 
meetings. We also integrate an E-learning system to enhance training efficiency. Each year, training programs are designed based on operational strategies and competency planning, with different training 
categories tailored for various positions. This approach ensures that employees can apply what they have learned to their work, improving work quality and efficiency.
●   Supervisor Training
Plan courses based on the assignments of supervisors at 
all levels, so that supervisors can learn tools and methods 
through training to strengthen on-site management.
●   Core Management
Required courses are planned for supervisors at different 
levels. Each year employees/supervisors recommended 
for promotion must complete the required relevant 
courses before recommendation to ensure that they are 
equipped with the core competencies required for the 
upcoming position.
●   Suggestion Reward
Encourage employees to identify abnormalities at work, 
propose good improvement plans, inspire employees' 
willingness to learn, and connect them with work 
practices.
●   Personal Development
Assist employees in career development and respect 
their job transfer will for employees to develop in 
coordination with the organization and arrange and 
plan the personal career to adapt to the changes in 
the environment and meet the needs for organizational 
growth.
●   Internal Instructor Training
Through the internal instructor training system, we 
develop and train quality instructors and accumulate a 
corporate knowledge heritage. Currently, there are 448 
internal instructors. Additionally, we thank and encourage 
internal instructors for their constant contribution to the 
Company and enhancement of internal teaching quality. 
Every year, we also commend instructors on Teacher’s 
Day.
●   Professional Competence Training
Through the required competence training and mentoring, 
work qualification certification, and external training, 
employees can receive systematic competence training. 
Additionally, in response to the advanced equipment, 
we progressively establish audio teaching materials for 
loader and unloader/unwinder and winder operations, 
HMI operations, routine checks, process maintenance, 
and works maintenance.
●   Direct Labor Training
Provide direct labor with qualification training on 
professional skills and machine operation to help them 
pass machine operation certification. The mentoring 
system is also arranged and rewards are planned 
for mentors to encourage them to given technical 
and practical instructions for direct labor to facilitate 
experience inheritance.
●   Orientation Training
To assist new employees in quickly integrating into 
the Company organization and culture (including key 
internal regulations, employee grievance procedures, 
compliance with regulations, and ESG E-learning), new 
recruits are required to complete an onboarding training 
program within 1 to 3 months, in addition to the first-day 
orientation course (In 2024, the completion rate for this 
training was 100%).
●   General Education Courses
Various courses are organized according to the government’s 
SHE regulations, ESG human rights training, workplace 
violence training, customers quality requirements, or the 
companys business development strategies.
●   Enhancement of Total Quality Awareness
Promote the improvement of quality awareness among 
plant personnel, and apply statistical process quality 
control methods to manage and improve process 
modules to enhance work quality and efficiency.

 4-6. Protection of Employee Rights and Interests
We are committed to developing a work-life balance atmosphere. In benefit design, we offer 
employees with comprehensive benefit plans better than the Standards Labor Act, such as leave; 
insurance; emergency assistance; cash gifts for weddings, funerals, and births; and shopping 
discounts at contracted stores. To ensure the rights and interests of employees, we establish all 
systems with legal compliance as the basic principle.
Appropriate Work Protection
Plants in Taiwan, mainland China, and Thailand give employees the freedom to terminate 
employment. However, to protect the right to work of employees, we prioritize transfer to replace 
resignation. If an employee cannot fit in their job and apply for resignation, apart from assigning 
related supervisors to interview these employees, the HR unit will interview each of them to 
understand their reason for resignation to arrange a job transfer or assistance as necessary. In 
addition to related benefits, we also pay employees during the notification period. In the event 
of significant operational changes, the Company will provide advance notice to employees 
in accordance with the regulations of the location where the operations are based, and offer 
necessary assistance, such as transferring employees to other internal units or helping them apply 
for relevant government subsidies.
Compeq provides its employees with social insurance as required by local regulations, and also 
offers a range of group insurance options at discounted rates, including critical illness insurance, 
medical insurance, accident insurance, and overseas travel insurance for business trips. These 
benefits are designed to ensure the safety and well-being of employees in both their work and 
personal lives. Additionally, employees have the option to extend these group insurance benefits 
to their dependents (parents, spouse, and children). Coverage continues during sick leave, and 
on-site insurance services are available within the Company to offer insurance consultations and 
application assistance, ensuring employees are well-informed about their insurance coverage and 
benefits.
Reliable Retirement System
To ensure a stable post-retirement life for its employees, the Company has established labor 
retirement regulations and formed a Labor Retirement Supervision Committee, which meets 
quarterly. For each full-time employee, the Company allocates (old scheme) or contributes 
(new scheme) retirement funds. Under the old scheme, 5% of the total monthly salary expense 
is regularly allocated to the retirement reserve fund and deposited in the Trust Department of 
Bank of Taiwan. At the end of the year, if the estimated account balance is insufficient to cover 
the retirement benefits for employees eligible to retire in the next year, the Company will make 
up the shortfall by the end of March of the following year. Additionally, the Company annually 
commissions actuaries to provide a Defined Benefit Actuarial Report to protect labor rights. Starting 
from July 1, 2005, the Company has concurrently adopted the government ’s new retirement 
scheme. Under this scheme, 6% of the employee’s salary will be contributed to their individual 
retirement pension accounts. For employees who voluntarily contributed to their account, the 
voluntary contribution rate will be deducted from their monthly salary and deposited into their 
personal retirement accounts with the Bureau of Labor Insurance.
In Taiwan, the Company also regularly offers favorable retirement plans. The pension base 
and payment standards will be calculated according to the Labor Standards Act. Additionally, 
employees eligible to receive pensions under the Labor Standards Act (old scheme) will receive an 
extra bases. This ensures that all employees can enjoy secure protection after retirement.
In accordance with the aforementioned relevant regulations, the company recognized pension 
costs of NTD 125,251 thousand in 2024. Additionally, the mainland China subsidiary and other 
foreign subsidiaries, in compliance with local laws, allocate pension insurance contributions 
monthly based on a fixed percentage of total local employee salaries. The recognized pension cost 
in 2024 was NTD 577,595 thousand.
Measures Better Than Legal Requirements
The Company offers a comprehensive and superior leave system compared to legal requirements. 
The benefits package includes various enhancements over the Labor Standards Act, such as 
leave, insurance, emergency assistance, marriage and bereavement allowances, maternity 
benefits, and discounts at partner stores. These provisions help employees achieve a balance 
between work and life, enabling them to focus on their work, remain long-term, and develop within 
the Company.
Project
Measures Better Than Legal Requirements
Paid Personal Leave/ 
Sick Leave
Paid personal leave and sick leave are entitled to personnel of 
related categories in Taiwan.

in Taiwan, better than the one-day paid compassionate leave.

To take care of female employees, plants in Taiwan offer maternity 
leave better than the legal requirements to employees with service 
less than 6 months.
Overtime Pay
Production line workers are paid at a multiple better than the legal 
requirements.
Other Benefits
Birthday gifts, holiday vouchers, travel subsidies, wedding cash 
gifts, maternity allowances, scholarships for children, hospital 
condolences, funeral condolences, emergency relief funds, etc.
For plants in mainland China, home purchase allowances are 
offered to engineers to help them settle down. We also provide 
them with the retention bonus.

 4-7. Labor-Management Relations
Compeq Labor Union
Compeq ’s Taiwan Plants established a labor union in 1979. The Huizhou and Suzhou Plants 
in China established unions in 2011 and 2010, respectively, while the Chongqing Plant has 
employee representatives and the Thailand Plant has Employee Welfare Committee. We respect 
the rights granted to employees by law, and union representatives are elected by the employees to 
communicate with company management. We do not prevent or interfere with employees’ freedom 
of association. At operational sites where labor union have not yet been established, all employees 
are equally protected by the rights granted to them under local laws.
By establishing labor unions and electing employee representatives, all employee rights can 
be fully protected. For instances, 88.2% of employees in Taiwan have joined the union and are 
protected by relevant regulations. The union operates by holding quarterly labor-management 
meetings, an annual general meeting, and monthly or ad-hoc board meetings. The topics and 
minutes of each meeting are posted on bulletin boards for employees to review. Additionally, group 
leader meetings are held occasionally to promote company and union policies and gather member 
feedback. The union also organizes various activities such as team-building events and employee 
care programs, ensuring employee rights are maintained and stable labor relations are upheld. 
Furthermore, labor education sessions are held quarterly, featuring external industry experts who 
conduct courses on workplace issues and physical and mental health to enhance employees’ 
awareness of labor-related matters.
At labor-management meetings, management can communicate the Company ’ s policies to 
employees, understand their needs, and reach a consensus. Likewise, employees can give 
feedback and recommendations to achieve labor-management harmony. Representatives from 
both sides also understand and discuss affairs that concern employees and make effective 
and feasible solutions. After each labor-management meeting, we disclose the minutes for all 
employees to understand the management’s responses to their problems.
Currently, a collective agreement has not yet been signed. The Company, in addition to listening 
to the union’s expressed desire to sign such an agreement, has also provided specific responses 
and explanations to the union’s inquiries. Both parties are communicating about the “necessity 
of signing a collective agreement” and understanding the union’s subsequent direction for the 
agreement’s signing and operation, with ongoing discussions.
Communication Channels
The Company values dialogue with employees and aims to understand their concerns through 
various communication channels, improving company policies and practices. Therefore, the 
Company has established multiple internal grievance and communication channels. Employees 
can express opinions or provide suggestions anonymously or by name. A MEMO is issued 
monthly to encourage employees to use these channels, which include “direct communication with 
supervisors”, “direct communication with HR units/supervisors”, “physical suggestion boxes”, 
“email”, “hotline”, “forums”, and “the union”. In the Taiwan Plant, communications for foreign 
employees are translated into their native languages and printed as posters posted in various 
areas, including the shoe-changing area, to achieve seamless communication with employees.

In addition to establishing comprehensive communication platforms, the Company 
continuously executes and improves communication enhancement projects 
to ensure the completeness and effectiveness of information dissemination 
to all employees. Compeq conducts investigations and provides feedback on 
employee opinions and grievance cases based on related issues. The Company 
also implements online education and training (such as email promotions and 
online quizzes). For instance, CSR communication skills courses are continually 
offered to supervisory personnel, including team leaders, section chiefs, and 
managers who directly manage on-site employees. The overall participation rate 
for those courses was 100%, helping supervisors understand current regulations, 
international labor standards trends, and the importance of CSR management. 
As a result, in recent years, the Company has not experienced any incidents or 
received any complaints related to forced or compulsory labor, nor has it faced any 
significant fines or non-monetary sanctions in the social and economic fields.
For grievance cases, investigations and subsequent improvements are carried out 
based on the issues related to the received cases. Additionally, a confidentiality 
mechanism has been established for employees involved in complaints or 
incidents to ensure the freedom and confidentiality of their complaints. Retaliation 
against complaints or those assisting with investigations is strictly prohibited, 
and any such incidents will be dealt with according to company regulations. In 
2024, a total of 1,225 employee feedback cases and 49 employee grievances 
were received internally. All cases have been communicated and resolved with 
appropriate improvement measures, achieving a 100% closure rate.
When handling employee grievances regardless, we make no discrimination based 
on race, religion, color, nationality, and gender. Opinion boxes and posters are 
also set up at work sites and in cafeterias to ensure that employees' opinions and 
needs are communicated and assisted in the most timely manner.
The feedback mechanism at the Thailand plant is not yet fully developed and has not been included in the statistics.

 4-8. Employee Welfare Measures
Compeq believes that a healthy and happy workforce leads to a highly 
productive enterprise. Therefore, the Company not only continues to improve 
employee welfare systems and provide a healthy and safe working environment 
but also focuses on creating a vibrant workplace from the employees
’ 
perspective. Employees are encouraged to express their creativity during 
work and leisure activities through diverse activity designs. Additionally, the 
Company has established an Employee Welfare Committee. The funding mainly 
comes from the Company’s operating revenue and the allocation of employee 
welfare funds from scrap sales, managed and utilized by representatives from 
both labor and management. Promoting harmonious relations between labor 
and management. The Company also plans a variety of benefits and activities 
every year, including travel, welfare products for three major festivals, birthday 
coupons, children's scholarships, group insurance, cultural and recreational 
activities, as well as childbirth and hospitalization subsidies.
Commendation of Senior Employees and Model Employees
Compeq expresses gratitude to every employee for their dedication and hard 
work, especially to senior employees for their perseverance over the years. 
Each year, employees with over 10 years of service (accumulated in 5-year 
increments, such as 15 years, 20 years) are awarded bonuses and medals to 
thank them for upholding the Company’s core values. In May of each year, a 
commendation event is held to honor exemplary employees, with a ceremony 
conducted at the plant and announcements made on the Company’s internal 
network to serve as a model for all. In 2024, a total of 1,885 long-service 
employee commemorative medals were awarded, and NTD 5.461 million in 
bonuses were distributed.
Comprehensive Employee Club Activities
Compeq’s welfare programs comply with or exceed local legal requirements. Some 
welfare items are adjusted based on regional differences. The Company respects 
employees ’ freedom of association and encourages them to develop personal 
interests and expertise through various clubs, such as billiards, jogging, ballroom 
dance, table tennis, badminton, board games, music, and photography clubs. Each 
club holds regular meetings and organizes various activities from time to time.

 4-9. Occupational Health and Safety (OH&S)
4-9-1. OH&S Management System
To enhance the overall safety and health system and management performance, the Company has 
been implementing the OHSAS 18001 management system since 2005. Through collective efforts, it 
has successively obtained OHSAS 18001 and TOSHMS certifications. Following the revision of the 
OHSAS management system, all sites, except for Suzhou and Thailand, have transitioned to ISO 
45001 certification. (relevant certificates can be viewed on the official website: https://www.compeq.
com.tw/duty04.php).
According to the operation of the management system, Compeq adheres to legal requirements, 
customer demands, and the Company’s sustainability principles to establish occupational safety 
and health management policies. The management system is designed with a focus on “prevention” 
as its central concept. The Company strictly complies with applicable occupational safety laws 
and related stakeholder requirements, continuously improving occupational safety and health 
performance to reduce the frequency rate (FR) and severity rate (SR) of disabling injuries, with the 
ultimate goals of achieving zero accidents (no major injuries).
Every year, we activate the regulation and hazard identification and risk assessment procedures, 
implement the electronic OH&S management system, and change management for any measure 
changes. We also assess the risk of high-risk operations and minimize risk severity through risk 
control. For example, we continuously arrange special health checkups for employees engaging 
in high-risk operations, including noise, ionizing radiation, etc. We also arrange graded health 
management for them according to the checkup results.

4-9-2. Worker Participation, Consultation, and Communication on Occupational Safety and Health
The Company has established Occupational Safety and Health Committee (Taiwan), Safety Production Committee (China), and EHS Committee (Thailand). The highest level of the safety and health 
management committee is the plant GM. Labor representatives can directly provide safety and health issues or feedback to department representatives or communicate directly with senior manager through 
the committee. For any emergency safety incidents, there are internal communication procedures in place for employees to report at any time. The Company values all communication from employees and 
ensures that no employee faces retaliation or punishment for reporting. The Occupational Safety and Health Committee meets regularly to discuss various safety and health issues, including occupational 
accident investigation reports. During these meetings, the safety and health unit regularly reports on various safety indicators. Discussions and planning are conducted using the PDCA cycle, focusing on 
potential or possible safety issues in the Company’s production process. The committee formulates relevant health and safety protections. Below is a summary of the organizational participation of labor 
representatives and the main discussion issues for 2024 in each region.
Note: Taiwanese regulations require that labor representatives constitute at least one-third of the total, at least one-half in Thailand. There are no such 
requirements in other regions.

4-9-3. Specific Measures for Occupational Safety
To strengthen the safety management of contractors entering the plant, 
Compeq has established relevant regulations, implementing measures 
such as contractor evaluation, pre-construction safety briefings, entry 
education and training, and high-risk operation controls to ensure that 
only qualified individuals are allowed to operate. In 2024, a total of 1,816 
safety training sessions (totaling 2,783 hours) were completed across the 
enterprise. There was one occupational injury reported in Taiwan and one 
in Thailand (both due to physical hazards). The related deficiencies were 
immediately rectified, and key focus areas have been fully addressed 
through awareness campaigns.
To continuously improve the working environment for our 
employees, we control temperature, humidity, lighting, noise, and 
toxic and hazardous substances starting from the design stage. 
We conduct inspections in accordance with occupational safety 
regulations (e.g., in Taiwan, 600 test points were checked, with 
1,876 internal audit deficiencies improved across the enterprise). 
We reviewed and compared annual data to ensure all indicators 
meet legal requirements.
Based on the Guidelines for Ergonomics 
Hazard Prevention Program, we establish 
the “Regulations for Assessment of 
Ergonomic Hazards” to prevent work-
related hazards, such as musculoskeletal 
disorders (MSDs), for employees. In 2024, 
apart from surveying 2,445 persons with a 
questionnaire, we also assessed different 
types of manufacturing processes and 
made improvements to provide employees 
with a more conformable and safer work 
environment.
To enhance the safety of personnel in handling chemicals, 
Compeq implemented strict control of Safety Data Sheets 
(SDS) for chemicals. We manage the safety of chemical usage 
and storage environment and regularly provide safety and 
health education and training to users. This training aims to 
raise awareness and ensure the safe use of chemicals. At the 
same time, based on new government measures for chemical 
management, we implement a tiered management system for 
chemicals within the plant. This system takes into account 
factors such as the type of working environment, the amount of 
chemicals used and stored, and the number of users. Currently, 
all chemicals in the plant fall under tier-one management, 
and we continually seek opportunities to improve the working 
environment or related equipment.
Since 2005, the Company has implemented a safety performance 
evaluation system, assessing each unit’s adherence to safety 
standards monthly and quarterly. Using a self-evaluation concept 
for rewards, units are encouraged to continuously improve. The 
system includes a progress award to promote and recognize 
safety practices in daily operations. In 2024, a total of 531 
motions were proposed, with award money amounting the NTD 
251 thousand.
To prevent occupational hazards and reduce health and 
safety risks, we have established the “Safety and Health 
Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment Procedures”. 
This procedure involves all units in identifying and 
evaluating hazardous factors, classifying them by risk level, 
and proposing control measures. This process aims to 
standardize the safety management of equipment, materials, 
and work procedures. In 2024, a total of 267 operational 
risk identification and assessment tasks were performed 
(Taiwan: 84; China: 183).
To enhance personal protection at work, we provide employees with 
PPE appropriate to their work and actual requirements. We also post 
eye-catching labels of the required PPE in respective regions. We also 
arrange courses on PPE use and respirator tightness check to provide 
employees with PPE training and supervise them on using its use to 
effectively enhance personal protection awareness in employees.
In addition to pre-employment physical examinations, the Company arranges regular 
health checkups as required by law and informs employees of the results. This includes 
general and specialized health checks. Health promotion activities are also conducted, 
with weekly health information sent to all employees. In 2024, a total of 3,847 general 
health checkups and 5,406 specialized health checks were conducted. The plant infirmary 
has a department of occupational medicine with professional physicians on-site, providing 
services such as occupational injury and illness assessment and consultation.

4-9-4. Workplace Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment
Upholding the spirit of prevention, zero accidents, and zero hazards, the industrial 
safety unit defines risk levels, sets controls and improvement targets for hazardous 
and risky operations, and includes them in the management records for periodic 
follow-up to continuously eliminate potential occupational hazards in the workplace 
and educate employees to leave the workplace to go to a safe place without 
worrying about being punished after detecting immediate hazards at work in 
additional to immediately reporting. In 2024, there was no sanction for doubts 
about safety reports.
To ensure the quality of hazard identification and risk assessment, in 2024 we 
selected senior onsite employees to help identify potential hazards and risks in 
the operating environment to increase employee participation in risk and hazard 
identification, assessment, and control, effectively enhance the effectiveness of 
hazard assessment, and form a safety culture. We also organized the plant-based 
hazard assessment competition to reward units with outstanding performance in 
hazard assessment, further the positive cycle of industrial safety management, and 
to prevent hazards.
Work Safety Promotion Projects
Project
Description
Effectiveness
Educational videos on fire 
prevention
Develop training materials on fire prevention and 
the use of flammable materials.
A video of approximately 7 minutes in length 
was produced and placed on the television walls 
of various departments for continuous 24-hour 
playback, in order to achieve disaster prevention 
memory reflex actions.
Replacement of Organic 
Solvent Containers in the 
Cleanroom with Metal 
Material and Grounding
To prevent the risk of electrostatic ignition, 
organic solvent containers in the cleanroom were 
replaced with metal material and grounding
The trash bins in the cleanroom have been 
replaced with new materials and properly 
grounded. Additionally, regulations for the use 
of organic solvent wiping cloths have been 
established to reduce the risk of fire.
Improvement of the 
pressing plate trolley anti-
pinch mechanism
Regarding the pressing plate trolley clamping 
points, the power supply location and the switch 
box location have been relocated to reduce the 
operation of clamping points.
The position of the pillar has been changed to be 
farther from the personnel operation interface, 
and warning signs have been installed to reduce 
the likelihood of occupational injuries.
Manual Chemical Dosing 
Improvement
Operators are required to carry buckets of 
chemical solution and pour them into the 
tanks, which poses a risk of splashing injuries. 
Improvements are to be made for dosing ports 
with a height of 1.2 meters or above.
Confirmation has been completed for 35 lines, 
with improvements made at 13 identified risk 
points.
Improvement of Pressure 
Resistance for VCP Line 
Elevation and Lowering Slot
There is a risk of being struck or caught when 
personnel enter the equipment at the VCP lifting 
and lowering trough for operations.
Modifications have been completed on 28 
lines (installation of anti-fall hooks and use of 
pressure-resistant support pillars).
Improvement of the Ink 
Removal Knife Adjuster 
on the Printing Machine to 
Prevent Hand Injuries
When adjusting the travel knob of the de-inking 
blade, personnel hold the position too low, which 
easily causes fingers to be pinched or injured 
by the scraper base of the operating printing 
machine.
Change the position of the de-inking blade stroke 
knob
Improvement of the Entry 
Point for Loading into the 
Green Paint Development 
Oven to Prevent Jamming
The side of the loading device at the feed inlet 
of the green paint developing oven lacks a guard 
plate, making it easy for personnel to accidentally 
insert their hands and get caught or injured.
Install a guard plate on the side of the feeding 
device to prevent personnel from reaching 
inside.
