4-9-5. Safety Audit and Improvement Projects
In addition to complying with the government regulations and internal SOPs and implementing 
automatic inspections and self-inspections, we also perform routine safety audits and unplanned 
spot checks and include the results in the industrial safety rating. We commend and reward 
outstanding performance to encourage personnel to engage in safety and health management. To 
enhance safety and health performance and reduce the loss of interests of related stakeholders, 
continuous promotion of the occupational safety improvement plan is underway. The plan aims 
to improve the effectiveness of safety audits through automated inspections and checks, while 
simultaneously reducing major occupational safety risks through engineering improvements.
In 2024, the main non-conformities identified during audits were primarily related to not wearing 
protective equipment, followed by the presence of flammable materials placed near ovens and 
electrical control boxes, as well as bypassing safety devices. Special attention was given to 
conducting risk hazard assessments for units with high risks of occupational injuries due to falling 
objects and ergonomic risks. Units were guided to independently identify risk areas and implement 
controlled improvements.
4-9-6. Food Safety
To address food safety risks, we develop methods for food safety management and supervision 
and provide safe, sanitary, and healthy foods, beverages, and dining environments to control food 
safety for employees. To ensure employee safety, a total of 7 sessions were conducted in 2024, 
with 192 participants involved in food poisoning drills to enhance emergency response capabilities.
4-9-7. Accident Investigation
At Compeq, we value the real-time reporting, investigation, and prevention of every accident. 
When an accident occurs to an employee or contractor, we will conduct accident investigation 
and follow up on the aftermath according to the Accident Handling and Investigation Management 
Regulations. We will also judge the status of damage and work-related injury based on the 
accident’s content. After accident investigation, responsible units will continuously supervise and 
follow up on the accident and include it as an example for industrial safety awareness education 
to reduce damage and prevent the recurrence of similar accidents. We have also established 
SOPs for handling close calls to notify each responsible units based on the incident handling and 
investigation regulations and processes to verify if there are incidents and conduct investigation. If 
there are any emergencies or close calls relating to industrial safety, we have also established the 
internal communication process for timely reporting.
4-9-8. Emergency Response Measures
To enhance emergency response capabilities, the Company has established emergency response 
procedures and set up emergency response teams at each plant. These teams develop response 
processes for various scenarios and conduct annual disaster response drills. In 2024, a total of 
1,008 emergency response drills were executed (including simulations for chemical disasters, 
toxic substances, hazardous materials, specific chemicals, evacuation drills, cylinder liquid leaks, 
special equipment rescue, and confined spaces), with 47,019 participants involved.
◆ Selection of qualified (e.g., HACCP) catering service providers to supply foods
◆ Daily inspection of food supply and request for compliance with the laws and 
regulations related to food safety and sanitation
◆ Regular health checkups for food suppliers. No one suffering from lung 
contagious diseases is allowed to perform their work
◆ Adjust the principle of side dishes for meals, reduce the number of deep-fried 
meals, and provide salad meals for personnel to choose from
◆ Regular kitchen safety and sanitation check and annual audit to verify 
compliance with food safety and sanitation regulations
◆ Strict request catering service providers not to use food ingredients of unknown 
sources
◆ Monthly water quality check of water dispensers and publishing examination 
results

4-9-9. OH&S education and training
For all employees, an annual education and training plan is arranged every year according 
to the safety and health related legislation and in-house requirements and is implemented as 
planned for employees to develop the awareness of hazards in the work environment and the 
OH&S knowledge and concepts required for disaster prevention to ensure that each employee is 
equipped with the correct safety and health concept.
In 2024, the Company conducted safety and health education and training for new and current 
employees, as well as emergency response and fire safety training through both internal and 
external courses. To enhance employee safety awareness and prevent disasters, “Practical Safety 
Training” was implemented, allowing employees to operate equipment, understand workplace 
hazards, and learn about potential accident causes and countermeasures. This initiative aims to 
develop a proactive safety mindset and reduce accidents caused by unsafe behaviors. In addition 
to scheduled training, ad-hoc training sessions were arranged for specific incidents or major 
deficiencies. A total of 22,541 participants received training in 2024, with a total of 351 thousand 
hours of training conducted, averaging 13.3 hours per person. All training was delivered in the local 
language and followed by assessments to evaluate effectiveness.
4-9-10. Fire Drills
To enhance employee awareness of emergency evacuation and firefighting, every year we 
organize firefighting task force training and emergency evacuation drills, such as the in-house 
emergency response and reporting procedures, commanding system, and handling of fires, gas 
leaks, chemical spills, odors, earthquakes, and radiation leaks with respect to related laws and 
regulations. These practical training and drills aim to equip employees with the awareness of fires 
and the ability to use firefighting equipment. With such drills, employees can evacuate in a safe 
and swift manner in case of emergency to reduce the loss of property and life from fires on the 
organizational premises.
Additionally, we design and build fire prevention and firefighting facilities strictly in accordance 
with the fire regulations and implement the “Fire Safety Accountability System” in workplaces 
for employees to carry out routine maintenance and management of fire safety facilities. We also 
hire quality fire services companies to maintain our fire system and outsource fire safety system 
inspections to third-party fire inspection organizations and implement periodic fire safety education 
and training and emergency response drills to enhance the fire safety awareness and emergency 
response capability of employees.

4-9-11. Occupational Accident Management
In 2024, Compeq continued to promote hands-on safety training and utilized intelligent auditing methods such as PAD for risk behavior warnings and corrections. Safety was prioritized to ensure that 
operational speed does not compromise safety. Occupational accident statistics for 2024, including those for employees and non-employee workers, are shown in the following chart. We adhere to legal 
requirements for reporting occupational accidents, with each plant reporting monthly injury statistics. In the event of an accident, the notification process is followed , and immediate investigation and 
improvement measures are implemented to prevent recurrence. Dedicated personnel monitor and track occupational hazards to keep the situation under constant review. In the management of non-Compeq 
employees, all plants manage resident employees of suppliers and contractors according to local laws and regulations currently in practice. According to the current legal framework and management 
model, there were no incidents in 2024 resulting in permanent disability or death of employees or workers due to occupational hazards. However, there was one case of occupational disease caused by 
improper lifting techniques. The primary cause was the small stature of the individual, who frequently lifted boards over the shoulder, leading to repetitive strain injuries to the tendons. An immediate parallel 
investigation into high-risk repetitive motions was initiated, assessing the posture, weight, and frequency of the lifting tasks through ergonomic evaluation to identify and mitigate potential hazards.
In 2024, no serious occupational injuries occurred; however, the overall disabling injury frequency rate (FR) and disabling injury severity rate (SR) of disabling injuries both declined compared to the previous 
year. The primary causes were personnel not following prescribed procedures and failing to pay necessary attention. To address these issues, ongoing safety interactions with personnel will be conducted to 
continuously promote safety awareness. Additionally, management inspections will be strengthened, and clear safety signs and instructions will be posted in areas prone to accidents to reduce the likelihood 
of workplace injuries. Regarding the condition of employees injured at work, the medical office, together with the factory's occupational medicine physicians, arranges weekly on-site visits and conducts 
assessments for job reassignment and return to work, in order to safeguard the health and safety of employees during operations.
Apart from traffic accidents during commuting, injury categories primarily involve incidents related to the work environment, with equipment entanglement and falling objects being more frequent. 
Investigations and root cause analyses have been conducted for each incident, and responsible units are tasked with developing appropriate improvement measures and prevention strategies to reduce 
risks for employees and workers. Additionally, for traffic accidents, we have enhanced employee traffic safety awareness and provided education and training.
●	 Reliable Accident Review and Publicity: In addition to site rectification, responsible units are requested to inventory operations and review risks again and revise SOPs as necessary for all accidents. 
Additionally, accident case studies are developed for publicity and education to prevent their recurrence.
●	 Periodic Gathering of Accident Analysis and Learning: For all plants to share experiences, learn lessons, and stay alert.
●	 Review and Standardization of Universal Operations: For common accidents in mechanical equipment (cuts and rolling) and electrical equipment (electric shocks), we review the universal operations 
across plants at the same time for all plants to make adaptive adjustments to enhance safety management efficiency.
●	 For injured employees, the infirmary and safety unit, together with the on-site occupational medicine doctor, arrange weekly visits to the plant and conduct return-to-work assessments to prevent any 
impact on the recovery of the injured area once employees resume work.

Conduct a risk assessment 
on the safety of material

the loading/unloading

before production can

production safety
In 2024, the indicators for occupational injuries and industrial safety incidents all exceeded the 
self-management targets. Compeq recognizes the need to accelerate improvement measures. 
Each work injury incident requires the responsible unit to review an 8D report, and for common 
issues, parallel project improvements are being promoted across all plants. The plant has 
implemented improvements following workplace injuries, including the addition of protective doors 
and safety sensors on the rack side of the sheet feeding machine, enhancements to the anti-
pinch measures on the press cart columns, correction of a bug that prevented the sheet feeding 
machine's light curtain from stopping during reset, and the installation of light curtains on the 
rapid roll-up doors. Every two weeks, case studies are produced and promoted, and meetings are 
held with on-site middle-level supervisors to link these with workplace safety inspection items. 
On-site personnel are required to carry out first-level autonomous safety inspections, and are 
encouraged to actively propose safety improvement suggestions to enhance overall workplace 
safety awareness.
In 2025, the focus will be on projects related to object falling, human factors engineering, and 
improvements in the reset procedures of the release mechanism. Continuous efforts will be made 
to include video playback audit items in the safety risk assessments and audit management for 
high-risk categories and units that have experienced occupational injury incidents.
Compliance with the Occupational Safety and Health Act
In 2024, Taiwan recorded a total of three violations of occupational safety and health regulations, 
primarily related to work-related injuries, resulting in fines totaling NT$500,000. In the future, we 
will continue to review each accident and penalty incident. We will progressively improve personnel 
safety awareness by focusing on high-risk hazardous operations, high-frequency false alarm 
events, and concentrated hidden dangers.

4-9-12. Workplace Health and Safety Activities
We value the health of employees. Therefore, we hire physicians and nurses at all plants in Taiwan 
to provide employees with healthcare services. We also hire health professionals at plants in 
mainland China and Thailand to plan the annual healthcare service program with nursing expertise 
and new concepts in health promotion. The program includes health checkups, anomaly follow-ups, 
and related health promotion events for all employees to access well-planned healthcare services. 
Every month we deliver the health e-newsletter by email and update to different publicity topics to 
remind employees of the importance of their own physical health.
Health Checkups and Management
Compeq collaborates with professional medical teams from Min-Sheng and Ten-Chan to offer 
employees free and non-discriminatory health checks. These annual health checks include general 
health checks for new and current employees, as well as specialized exams for specific work 
environments (e.g., high noise, dust, X-ray). In 2024, a total of 9,253 health checks were conducted 
(Taiwan plants: 4,156 people, China plants: 4,559 people, Thailand plant: 538 people), achieving a 
100% participation rate.
The Taiwan plant conducted 1,210 pre-employment physical examinations, 1,062 annual general 
health checkups, 284 special physical examinations for new employees, and 1,600 annual special 
health checkups. After the health checkups, plant health professionals help with medical referrals 
and periodic examinations and care services for important anomalies found in the health checkups 
after combining the monthly overtime hours and health risk assessment of employees. They also 
arrange re-checkups or referral to general hospitals for more detailed examinations as necessary. 
Additionally, we arrange individual health consultation services based on the analysis of past health 
checkup data for employees to better understand their health condition and continuously follow up 
on various ill-health items for “early detection and early intervention”.
We also proactively collaborate with the local health authorities to arrange free cancer screening 
(e.g., oral cavity cancer, colon cancer, cervical cancer) and influenza vaccination to reduce the 
infectious diseases from spreading. The personal health and service records and information 
of each employee will only be used for assessing if an employee is located in a safe workplace 
environment and will not be used for other purposes. These records and information will be 
properly kept by the responsible health management unit without leakage. In addition, we provide 
project counseling for employees in need. In 2024, no employees requested the services.

Workload Prevention and Occupational Disease Prevention Management
Compeq’s plants manage high-risk duties and occupational disease prevention according to local regulations. In Taiwan, to monitor labor working conditions and assess exposure, environmental 
measurements are conducted in accordance with occupational safety regulations. Data is reviewed annually to assess various indicators, ensuring that working environments meet legal requirements. 
Additionally, for employees engaged in high-risk duties, specialized health examinations and a tiered health management system are implemented in accordance with legal requirements.
The Company actively manages diseases triggered by abnormal workloads (such as noise and dust). In 2024, the Taiwan region completed assessments of abnormal workloads and conducted interviews 
and follow-ups with high-risk personnel. In China region, pre-employment, in-service, and post-employment physical examinations are conducted according to regulations. Employees with occupational 
contraindications are reassigned as required, and no occupational diseases were reported in 2024.
Compeq holds annual health management result meetings, establishes mechanisms for potential reporting and care, and tracks abnormal cases while reviewing high-risk groups. Physicians are scheduled 
for on-site visits and observations to provide suggestions and improvements. The focus is on identifying high-risk groups early, eliminating hazard exposure factors at the source, and using personal 
protective equipment as the last line of defense. This approach, combined with comprehensive environmental monitoring and health risk classification management, aims to create a healthier and more 
comfortable working environment. In 2024, a total of 243 health consultation sessions were conducted.

Health Promotion Activity
Health promotion is health empowerment for employees. Through health promotion, employees are 
given access to correct health knowledge to develop a positive attitude toward health and personal 
health promotion behavior to eventually build a sound lifestyle. Therefore, Compeq plans various 
health promotion activities tailored to the characteristics of each plant to enhance employees' 
physical and mental well-being, help them better understand their rights and obligations, and 
develop their self-rescue and mutual aid capabilities. In 2024, a series of health promotion activities 
were organized.

Compeq has long been dedicated to advancing social welfare initiatives. We not only care about 
the underprivileged groups in society, but are also committed to cultivating the talent needed by 
the PCB industry. Compeq supports relevant projects through financial donations and encourages 
employees to actively participate in volunteer activities. We will continue to invest in social welfare 
to realize the contribution of Compeq to society.
 5-1. Friendship Maintenance with Local Communities and 
Local Contributions
Compeq's Dayuan, Suzhou, and Chongqing plants are located in local industrial parks and thus 
have no community in the surrounding areas. For the Luzhu and Huizhou plants, we assessed the 
local environment and community based on local government and regulatory requirements before 
construction and ensured compliance with local regulations.
Compeq's Luzhu Plant is located in the Xinzhuang Neighborhood of Luzhu District, Taoyuan City. 
The Company views the community as the soil in which it is rooted. We believe that success 
is not solely due to our own efforts, without strong community relations, we would lose our 
foothold. By fostering a positive relationship with the community and society, we aim to thrive in 
a friendly environment. In response to the UN SDGs, Compeq adheres to the principle of "giving 
back to society what we take from it" and actively promotes three main areas of "Community 
Engagement," "Care for the Underprivileged," and "Environmental and Ecological Conservation." 
We extend our influence from the plant to the broader community, partnering with social welfare 
organizations, educational institutions, and other partners to inject positive energy into society and 
the environment, driving social progress and bringing warmth to more people, moving toward the 
goals of mutual advancement and integration.
● Support local communities environmental 
cleanup, disinfection work, and appreciation 
of environmental volunteer teams. Continue 
giving back to the communities by adopting 
road cleaning and greening near the plant, 
providing a high-quality environment and 
cityscape.
● Continue donating to community watches, 
volunteer police, civil defense, and fire units 
for project development. Through various 
efforts, create a harmonious society.
In 2024, we continued to promote donations to 
child welfare, emergency relief, and disability 
organizations in Taiwan, and regularly collected 
materials for donations. In addition, we make 
charitable donations to local elementary schools 
on a regular basis in China every year and 
encourage our colleagues to actively participate 
in various charitable activities.

 5-2. Social Engagement and Influence
In addition to directly participating in social welfare through project sponsorships and public 
donations, the Company gives back to society from time to time, strengthening the connection 
between the Company and the community, and demonstrating our sense of social responsibility, 
while also encouraging employees to actively participate and respond.
We will continue to deeply engage with the local community and care about the lives of our 
surrounding neighbors. Through participation in social activities, the Company has established 
neighborhood committees to build mutual trust and support with residents through visits and 
communication. We also focus on supporting the elderly, children, and other underprivileged 
groups by assisting local or reputable social welfare organizations in organizing festival 
celebrations or charity flea markets. We encourage employees to serve as environmental 
volunteers, contributing to the community and the planet. Our goal is to give back to society through 
specific actions, spreading love and hope throughout the community, and fostering a sense of unity 
between the plant and the neighborhood.
Participation in Social Welfare
Funds and materials are key resources for Compeq's public welfare activities. Besides regularly 
initiating charitable actions to bridge resource gaps, we participate in community celebrations 
each year, aligning with these events to establish communication channels with local residents. 
Additionally, we make donations and engage in interactions through local temple festivals.
● Sharing love and caring for the underprivileged: Compeq has long focused on supporting 
underprivileged groups and education. We regularly sponsor and donate to various 
organizations, including the Apple Charity Foundation, Yu-De Children's Home, SOS Children's 
Village, Kindness Value Social Welfare Association, Reindeer Children’s Home, and LOHAS 
Preschool. In 2024, we contributed approximately NTD 4.45 million.
● Responding to local activities: We support the establishment of a recorder ensemble at Sinjhuang 
Primary School in the Luzhu District to develop characteristic education. To enhance the fun 
and quality of recorder learning, we have hired professional teachers for advanced training and 
participation in competitions and performances, increasing the diversity of learning experiences. 
We provide an annual development fund of NTD 200,000 for the recorder ensemble, supporting 
their activities and local educational events such as graduation ceremonies and sports 
events, thereby aiding in the development of local education. In China, we also sponsored the 
establishment of a student development fund, educational enhancement expenses, and repairs 
for special education schools, the construction of a new comprehensive teaching building at 
Huzhen Middle School, as well as the renovation of love classrooms in Boluo County, Huizhou, 
Guangdong Province. In 2024, the total sponsorship amounted to approximately NTD 5.65 
million.
Community Impact Assessment
We care for the local communities where our plants are located. Hence, we assess the impact on 
local communities right at the beginning of plant construction, including environmental monitoring 
and disclosure, defining the relevant monitoring categories, and establishing the environmental 
monitoring plans. After plant construction, we also continue to maintain sound interaction and 
communication with local communities and governments. In addition to sending PR personnel to 
proactively visit nearby residents, we have also established the stakeholder report platform (https://
www.compeq.com.tw/relationship.php) and report the interaction status regularly to maintain total 
compliance with the environmental and social regulations and minimize negative impacts.
● Achievements:
● Compeq's long-term ongoing sponsorship ensures the recorder ensemble has sufficient resources to 
purchase instruments, hire professional instructors, and successfully conduct group rehearsals and 
performances.
● Enables more students to access music education equitably, bridging disparities between cities and 
rural areas as well as between schools.
● Potential Benefits:
● Through participation in the recorder ensemble, students enhance their musical literacy and teamwork 
capabilities, with opportunities to participate in on-campus and external arts performances and 
competitions, demonstrating their learning outcomes.
● The recorder ensemble becomes a key arts program within the school, enriching the school's curriculum 
and activities, strengthening the school's arts culture, and enhancing the school's visibility within the 
community.
Sinjhuang Primary School Recorder Ensemble

● Achievements:
● Kindness Value Social Welfare Association (Indigenous Children and Youth in Fuxing 
District): The establishment of the tribal Mqas (Happiness) parent-child corner assists 
the organization in providing group activities, cultural experience programs, and parent-
child education courses for children in remote or disadvantaged areas, offering children 
and youth a space for recreation and learning after school.
● Full Stomach Program: Addresses the issues of children in remote areas having 
nowhere to go after school and insufficient dinner provisions by providing funding to 
establish parent-child centers that offer safe spaces, snacks, and evening meals.
● Reindeer Children's Home: Sponsorship enables the organization to continuously 
improve facility infrastructure (24 flame-retardant curtain installations, 12 electrical 
cabinet installations, 18 outdoor chairs), expand service capacity, strengthen academic 
tutoring and life skills development, and enhance overall care quality.
● Potential Benefits: Sponsorship not only directly improves the living conditions and 
development opportunities for disadvantaged children but also helps them escape 
difficult circumstances and promotes self-sufficiency.

Product Lifecycle 
Management
TC-HW-410a.1
Percentage of products by revenue that contain IEC 62474 declarable 
substances
We periodically update the HS management regulations in response to 
the environmental protection and restrict substances regulations and do 
not use the chemicals concerned by IEC 62474. Hence, the percentage 
of products by revenue that contain IEC 62474 declarable substances 
was zero.
-
Supply Chain 
Management
Percentage of eligible products, by revenue, meeting the requirements for 
EPEAT registration or equivalent
We omitted this part because our products are not end products; hence, 
we are unable to pass the EPEAT registration for end-user electrical 
and electronic products. However, we will apply for verification and 
certification under the standards of existing ecolabels.
-
Materials 
Sourcing
Percentage of eligible products, by revenue, certified to an energy 
efficiency certification
We omitted this part because our products are not end products, and 
this standard does not apply.
